               THE FOOTBALL
        ASSOCIATION, LIMITED

  The A ssociation has been incorporated under the
C om pan ies A cts in order to facilitate the carrying
out o f its ob jects.


  The    Articles        of    Association   provide   that   the
Share Capital       shall consist of £100 divided into
2,000   Shares      of        5 pence   each.   A Shareholder
is not entitled to any dividend, bonus or profit.

               COUNCIL MEETINGS
     S T A N D IN G O R D E R S FO R T H E C O N D U C T OF B USIN ESS
                    AT M E E T IN G S O F T H E C O U N C IL




1.    Meetings o f Council
    All meetings o f the Council shall be held at eleven (11)
o ’clock in the morning, at the Head Office o f the Association,
except under special circumstances, when the Chairman or
the Council may fix some other hour or place. Meetings o f the
Council shall be restricted to not more than five (5) a season
(excluding Summer Meeting) and be held on such dates as the
Council shall decide annually at the first meeting held after
the Annual General Meeting. The Council or Emergency
Committee may arrange additional meetings or cancel a
meeting at their discretion. A record shall be kept o f the
attendance o f Members at each meeting.

2.    Notice of Meetings— Agenda
   T h e S e creta ry shall give seven (7) d a y s notice to each
M e m b e r o f every mee ting of the Cou nc il, to get her with
A g e n d a o f the business.

3.    Notices o f Motions
    N otice s o f all intended m o ti o n s shall be given in writing to
the S e cretary not less th a n fourteen (14) d a y s before the
meeting o f the Council. T h e Secretary shall place the notices
on the A g e n d a in the o r d e r received.
   A ll proposals o f C om m ittees and M embers o f the C o u n ­
cil involving any alteration o f Rules and Regulations o f The
Football A s s o c ia tio n shall, after Council has decided the
policy, be referred to the Rules R ev isio n Com m ittee for
their consideration and report before being finally adopted
by the Council.

4.    Order of Proceedings
   (i) M inutes
   At all meetings o f the C o u n c il the S e cretary shall present
the M inutes of the last p r eceding C ounc il meeting.
18                       S T A N D IN G ORDERS



     (ii) Correspondence
   The Secretary shall read such letters as may be necessary
or that any Member o f the Council desires to have read.
     (iii) Reports o f Committees
    The Reports of Committees shall next be considered; the
Chairman of each Committee or in his absence a Member of
the Committee, shall propose the adoption of the Report and
Members may then speak on any matter mentioned in the
Reports or move a resolution thereon.
   Q u estion s m ay be asked o f which notice is given in writ­
ing n o t less than three ( 3 ) days before the meeting o f the
Council.
   Verbal Reports o f m eetings o f Com m ittees which have
n o t been circulated shall be regarded as for information
only unless, on grounds o f urgency, an immediate decision
is necessary, in which case action recom m ended in such
Reports may be proceeded with immediately if the Council
gives its specific consent.
     (iv) The Business
  The business on the Agenda shall be proceeded with in such
order as the Chairman may direct.

5.   Mode of Discussion
   Each Member on speaking shall rise and address himself to
the Chairman, and not to any other Member of the Council.
   During the time any Member is speaking, all the other
Members shall remain seated, unless a Member rises to a
point of order.
   Whenever the Chairman rises to speak, no one shall
continue standing, nor shall anyone rise until the Chair has
been resumed.

6.     Mode of Proceeding with Motion
   All motions, whether original ones or amendments, shall, if
the Chairman requests it, be reduced to writing, signed by the
mover, and handed to the Secretary immediately on being
moved and every Member proposing such motion or
amendment shall read the same before speaking on it.
                       S T A N D IN G ORDERS                  19

7.   Order of Speaking
    The mover o f every original Resolution, but not o f any
amendment (unless it becomes an original motion), shall have the
right to reply, not introducing therein any new matter, but
confining himself strictly to the answering of previous
objections, immediately after which the question shall be put
from the Chair.
    N o other Member shall be allowed to speak more than
once on the same question, unless permission be given to
explain, or the attention o f the Chairman be called to a point
o f order.


8.   Amendments
   When an amendment is moved upon a proposition, no further
amendment shall be moved or taken into consideration until the
first is disposed of, but any number of amendments may be
brought forward in succession, and the question must be put in
such a manner that if one amendment be negatived another may
be moved upon the original proposition, but if an amendment be
affirmed it shall form the proposition under consideration,
whereupon further amendments may be moved, and if after the
disposal of an amendment no second or further amendment be
moved, the question must ultimately be put upon the original or
amended proposition, as the case may be, in order to its being
passed as a Resolution.


9.  Discussion on Amendments
  When discussion arises upon an amended proposition, the
mover of the amendment which has displaced the original
proposition may speak in reply, and so in like manner with
respect to any further and displacing amendments.


10.   Voting
   All questions shall be determined by a show o f hands,
unless either (a) a ballot, or (b) the recording of votes, be
requested by any Member supported by at least two (2) other
Members, and in the event o f votes being recorded under (b),
the names for, and against, shall be registered by the
Secretary and entered in the Minutes.
20                            S I A N D I N C ORDKKS

the wh ol e C o u n ci l , an d whilst in C o m m i t t e e , t here shall be no
rest ri ct i on as to the n u m b e r o f ti mes a M e m b e r m a y s peak to
t he qu est io n .

17.   Urgent Business
    M atter which is not on the A g en d a or S upplem entary
A genda shall not be considered by the Council unless,
without discussion, a m ajority o f three-fourths (|) o f the
M embers present by vote consent.
    M atters which the C h a irm a n decides should not be issued
with the O rd in ary A g en d a m ay be issued as “ S upplem en­
ta r y ” and any m atters th a t the C ouncil decide not to publish
in the printed M inutes shall be w ritten in the M inute Book.

18. Rescinding Resolution
   A Resolution shall not be rescinded at the M eeting o f the
Council at w hich it has been passed, unless the m otion to
rescind shall be carried by three-fourths (f) o f the M em bers
present and voting.
   N o m atter which has been discussed by the C ouncil, and
on which a Resolution has been passed, m a y be bro u g h t up
again for discussion within a period o f twelve (12) m onths
from the date on which the Resolution w as passed unless the
motion to discuss shall be carried by three-fourths (|) o f the
M embers present and voting.

 Executive Committee
     (a)     To have the full powers of the Council to make
 decisions upon all m atters o f policy and procedure to be
followed by The Association including those which require
immediate attention between Meetings of the Council when it
is inopportune to call a special Council meeting.
    (/?) To have power to appoint an Emergency Committee
consisting of the Chairman and Vice-Chairman of The Football
Association and the President of The Football League, or their
appointed Deputies. They shall have full powers to act on behalf
        . Council on routine mailers Ihal require attention and to
appoint Commissions.

       (c)    To review all matters of policy and to formulate any new
    policy for the consideration of the Council and to make such
    recommendations to the Council as it considers appropriate.
       (a)     To meet as and when considered necessary in the
    intervals between Council meetings.
       (e) To have power to co-opt to any meeting of the
    Com mittee up to three (3) Members with specialist
    knowledge when subjects of a specialist nature are being
    discussed.

    ( b) Matches with Foreign Associations, Leagues and
  Clubs*
     Associations, Leagues and C lubs, M em bers o f The
 A ssociation, wishing to play A ssociations, Leagues or Clubs
 o f another nationality, must apply to T he A ssociation for
 consent at least fourteen (14) days before the date o f the
 intended match.
     T he A ssociation will inform the other A ssociation
  concerned when consent has been given for m atches applied
 for.
     Associations, Leagues and their Clubs must not pay a
 com mission o f m ore than ten per cent (10% ), or the
 reim bursem ents o f travelling expenses, to organisations or
 persons arranging their tours.
    W here a N ational A ssociation provides in its Rules for the
 M em bership o f all Associations, Leagues, and Clubs within
 its area, consent for m atches with unaffiliated A ssociations,
 Leagues or Clubs will not be given.

participation in Sunday Football shall be taken as consent to
play on Sundays, except w hen C hristm as D a y be on a
.Sunday.

appropriate parent A ssociation, no m atch at which gate

te am s is a scratch team.

     M em orandum of Association of
   TH E FO O T B A L L A SSO C IA T IO N ,
                LIM IT E D

   1. The name of the Association is “ T H E F O O T B A L L
A SSO CIATION , L IM IT E D .”
  2. The Registered Office of the Association will be situate in
England.
   3. T he objects for which the Association is established
are:—
   (1) to acquire an d un d ertak e the properties an d liabilities
and to effectuate and c a rry into execution the powers,
obligations, duties, and general objects o f the present
Football A ssociation;
   (2) to p ro m o te the gam e o f A ssociation F ootball in every
w ay in which the A ssociation or the Council o f the
A ssociation shall think proper, and to take all such steps as
shall be deemed necessary or advisable for preventing
infringements o f the Rules and L aw s o f the G am e , or other
im proper m ethods or practices in such gam e, and for
protecting it from abuses;
   (3) to m ake, adopt, vary, and publish Rules, Regulations,
Bye-Laws and Conditions for the regulation o f the said game
or otherwise, and to tak e all such steps as shall be deemed
necessary or advisable for enforcing such Rules, Regulations,
Bye-Laws and Conditions;
   (4) to maintain, continue, or provide for the affiliation of
Associations and Clubs for promoting or playing Association
Football, and to take over and continue the present Register of
such Associations and Clubs as kept by The Football
Association;
 74              MEMORANDUM OF ASSOCIATION


      (5) to m aintain, continue, or provide for the registration o f
  Association Football Players and to take over and continue the
  present Registers of such Players as kept by The Football
  A ssociation;
     (6) to take over and continue with such variations as from

 docum ents o f The F ootball A ssociation;

      10. N o s h a r e q u a lif ic a tio n sh all b e r e q u i r e d f o r th e e le c tio n of
 a n y R e p r e s e n t a t i v e , b u t n o R e p r e s e n t a t i v e sh a ll b e e n t i t le d to

 t h e h o l d e r o f at l e a s t o n e (1) s h a r e .
     11. (a) N o person shall be entitled to be or to continue a
 Member of The A ssociation unless he is either an Officer of
 The A ssociation, a Member o f the Council or a Represen­
 tative of som e Division, affiliated Association or Member
 Club or a Member o f the Committee o f M anagement o f The
 Football League, Limited.
     ( b)   Any share held by any person who is not so entitled as
  aforesaid or who has ceased to be so entitled as aforesaid or in
  excess of the number to which he is so entitled as aforesaid shall
  be held in trust for such person or persons as the Council may
  direct and in such case the registered holder or his personal
  representatives or trustee in bankruptcy (as the case may be)
  shall upon request transfer such shares accordingly and shall on
  such transfer be entitled to be paid by the transferee that amount
  (if any) at the time of such transfer paid up on such shares and if
  no amount shall at that time be so paid up then shall not be
  entitled to any payment.
 86                          ARTICLES OF ASSOCIATION



    12. N o v o te sh all be giv en o r a llo w e d at a n y M e e ti n g by any
p e r s o n in r e s p e c t o f a n y s h a r e t h a t he is n o t e n t i t l e d to h o ld o r to
c o n ti n u e to h o ld u n d e r th e fo r e g o in g A r tic le .

   13. Transfers of shares shall be in writing in the usual
common form. The Council may in their absolute discretion and
without giving any reason refuse to register the transfer of any
share to a person of whom they shall not approve (whether or not
such share is fully paid); but shall in any such case within two
(2) months after the date on which the transfer was lodged
with The Association send to the transferee notice in writing
of the refusal.

   15. Whenever a right to call for a transfer of a share has
arisen the Council may authorise the Secretary to execute a
transfer thereof and a transfer so executed shall be as valid and
effective as if the same had been executed by the registered
holder of the share and the transferee shall be entered in the
Register as the holder thereof accordingly.

   2 4 . At any adjourned General Meeting originally
convened by the Council with or without requisition from
Members, the Members present, whatever their number
provided they shall not be less than five (5), shall have power
to decide on all matters which might have been disposed o f at
the Meeting from which the adjournment took place if a
quorum had been present thereat provided that three (3)
days’ notice must be given to the Members o f such
adjournment in order to enable special business to be
transacted thereat by less than a quorum.                    "
  2 5 . The President if present or if absent one (1) o f the
Vice-Presidents shall preside as Chairman at General
Meetings o f the Association.

     26. I f a t a n y M e e t i n g t h e r e b e n o su c h C h a i r m a n p r e s e n t

 n u m b e r to be C h a irm a n .

   2 7 . The Chairman may with the consent of the Meeting
 adjourn any Meeting from time to time and from place to place,
 but no business shall be transacted at any adjourned Meeting,
 other than the business left unfinished at the Meeting from which
 the adjournment took place.

all the Members entitled to vote at the Meeting or holding shares

all the shares conferring a right to vote at the Meeting) it shall be
taken in such manner and either forthwith or at such time not
being less than seven (7) days, and not more than fourteen (14)
days after the date of the Meeting, as may be determined by the
Chairman; and the result of such Poll shall be deemed to be the
Resolution of The Association in General Meeting. Any such Poll
 may be taken by voting papers sent to each M ember, stating the
proposed Resolution and giving instructions as to voting in
 respect thereof. A scrutineer or scrutineers of such voting papers
 shall be appointed by the Chairman, and the result of the voting
 thereby ascertained shall be deemed the Resolution of the
 Meeting on the subject in question. The mere pendency of a Po
 shall not prevent the continuance, if practicable, of the Meeting
 for other business.
     29.    Votes may be given either personally or by proxy. A proxy
  need not be a M ember of The Association.
     30 The instrument appointing a proxy shall be in writing
  under the hand of the appointer of his attorney duly authorised in
  writing and if such appointer is a corporation either under seal or
  under the hand of an Officer or attorney duly authorised.

    R E G U L A T IO N S OF A SSO C IA T IO N
          REGULATIONS FOR THE SANCTION AND
        CONTROL OF LEAGUES AND COMPETITIONS
        EXCEPT COMPETITIONS UNDER THE DIRECT
            JURISDICTION AND CONTROL OF
              THE FOOTBALL ASSOCIATION
    1. Clubs forming a League or Com petition, all o f which
are M em bers o f one (1) C ounty A ssociation only,* shall
m ake application for sanction to, and the League or
Com petition shall be sanctioned by* and be under the
jurisdiction o f that Association.
    2. Clubs forming a League or Com petition consisting of
C lubs within the area of, or affiliated to, tw o (2) or three (3)
C ou nty Associations, shall m ake application for sanction to
any o f such Associations. T he A ssociation to which
application has been m a d e shall within fourteen (14) day s of
its receipt submit the application to the other Association or
Associations concerned. T he League or Com petition shall be
sanctioned by, and be under the jurisdiction of, a C om m ittee
o f not less than tw o( 2) M em bers o f each Association.

    3. C lu b s f o r m i n g a L e a g u e o r C o m p e ti tio n c o n s is tin g
o f C lu b s w ith in th e a r e a o f m o r e t h a n th r e e (3) C o u n t y
A s s o c i a ti o n s , shall m a k e a p p lic a tio n f o r s a n c tio n to , a n d
th e L e a g u e o r C o m p e t i t i o n shall be s a n c tio n e d by, a n d be
u n d e r th e j u r is d i c ti o n of, T h e F o o tb a l l A s s o c i a ti o n , u nle ss
T h e A s s o c i a t i o n d ire c ts t h a t th e L e a g u e o r C o m p e ti tio n
m a y be s a n c ti o n e d u n d e r R e g u la tio n 2. A n a n n u a l s a n c tio n
fee w ill b e d e t e r m in e d by T h e A s s o c i a ti o n .
    4. A C o m p e ti tio n m a y be use d f o r t r a d e o r a d v e rtisin g
p u r p o s e s a n d th e n a m e o f th e d o n o r o f a C u p o r T r o p h y o r
an y o th e r p e r s o n m a y f o r m p a r t o f th e title o f a C o m p e ti tio n
on ly w ith th e p r i o r c o n s e n t o f T h e A s s o c i a t i o n o r a p p r o p r i ­
a te C o u n t y A s s o c i a ti o n .

H h e Army Football Association, The Royal Navy Football Association, The Royal
Air Force Football Association, The Amateur Football Alliance and The English
Schools’ Football Association are County Associations within the meaning of these
Regulations.
                                                            v •     -■■■- ■




                L E A G U E S A N D C O M P E T IT IO N S



   5. A Cup or Trophy presented to a Competition shall be
vested in the Association or Associations sanctioning the
Competition, as Trustees. If a Competition be discontinued from
any cause, the C u p or T rophy shall be returned to the donor
if the conditions attached to it so provide, held in trust, or
otherwise dealt with as the Association or Associations may
decide.

   6. The sanctioning Association or Associations may not allot
a Club to a League but may permit a League to make provision in
its Rules to restrict the number of Competitions, in addition t o
the F.A. and County Competitions, in which its Clubs take part.

  7. A Player without a written contract is not restricted as to
the Clubs for which he may play, provided he complies with the
Rules and Regulations of any Competition in which his Club or
Clubs may be engaged.

  8. A League or Competition may promote and manage
Competitions restricted to Clubs playing in its League or
Competition. A separate application must be made and consent
obtained for each Competition.

  9. Application for sanction of a League or Competition
(other than a Charity Competition) shall be m ad e on a form
m arked “ D ,” as scheduled to the Rules o f T he Football
Association. Tw o (2) copies o f the proposed Rules must
accom pany the application.

   10. Application for sanction of a Charity Competition
shall be m ade on a form m arked “ E ,” as scheduled to the
Rules o f T he Football Association. T w o (2) copies of the
proposed Rules must acco m pan y the application.

   11. When an application for sanction is made by a Junior
League or Competition under Regulations 1 and 2, the
Association or Associations concerned may require that the
Rules of the League or Competition shall provide that a Member
of the County Association or Associations shall sit upon the
Committee of the League or Competition. This arrangement
shall be for the guidance and instruction of the League or

          REGULATIONS FOR THE REGISTRATION
              AND CONTROL OF REFEREES

 Registration
 1. (a) Except by permission o f The Football Association or a
 C o u n ty Association, no person shall officiate as a Referee in
 any Competition u nder the jurisdiction of The Football
 Association unless he or she* is registered with a County
 Association or Service Association.
   (b) A Referee must be registered with the County Association
 within whose area he resides and may be required to pay an
annual subscription, subject thereto, he may also be registered
 with any other County Association on payment of the
subscription fixed by such Association. In cases where the
boundaries of County Associations overlap, the Counties
concerned m ay mutually agree about the registration o f
Referees within the overlapping areas. (See Section 7) A
Referee who changes his residence from ohe C o u n ty to
another shall not be required to pay a registration fee to his
new Association during the current season but must register
with the C ounty A ssociation into whose area he moves. That
C ounty shall then be his parent Association and shall deal
with all matters concerning him as a Referee. (This regulation
shall not apply to a Referee belonging to the Services’
Associations and The A m a te u r Football Alliance.)
  The Football Association or the relevant County Football
Association shall be responsible for the recruitment, training,
qualification and registration o f Referees, but m ay arrange
for the co-operation o f such bodies as the Referees’
Association and Referees’ Societies in these activities.
  (c) Referees appointed to matches by Associations or
Competitions under the jurisdiction of The Football Association
must be registered with a County Association but Competitions
or Clubs may agree for some other person to act in an
emergency.
  (d) Referees shall not be registered until they are able to satisfy
the County Association of their date of birth.

‘ W henever the word “ h e ” appears in these Regulations read “ he or
  sh e ” . For “ him ” read “ him or h e r” , etc.
                             REFEREES                           113


 Examination
 2. (a) All candidates shall be examined as to their suitability
 to officiate. A candidate failing to pass an examination may
 not present himself a second time within a period of three (3)
m o nths unless his exam iner recom m ends otherwise. T he
initial exam ination shall be both oral and written in the form
prescribed by T he F o otball A ssociation and shall include an
eyesight an d colour test by the card issued by T he Football
Association. After passing a n examination a cand idate shall
be advised by his C o u n ty A ssociation o f the Leagues and
Com petitions with w hich he m a y obtain appointm ents.
   (b) The Regulations of the Services’ Associations provide that
none but Servicemen shall be examined or classified by the
Service Association. All other County Associations are
requested to inform the Service Association concerned should
they examine a Serviceman.
Classification
3. (a) Each C ounty A ssociation shall, on or before the first
(1st) June in each year, classify their Referees according to
the reports received during the previous season as follows:—
      Class 1: Referees w ho have attained and maintained the
   standard necessary for this senior classification and have not
   to be included in the Special List as Class lx or Class 2x (see
   below) and those who have been promoted from Class 2 for
   outstanding ability.
     Class 2: Referees, w hose ages do not exceed fifty (50)
   w ho are senior but not o f the qualifications necessary for
   Class 1 and those who have been p rom oted from Class 3’
   for outstanding ability.
       Class 3: All other Referees not included in Class 1 and Class
  2.
   Class 3 (Youth): To include ages between 14 and 16 as at
the 1st o f A u gust o f ea ch season. A Class 3 (Youth Referee)
would au tom atically becom e a Class 3 Referee on his
Sixteenth birthday.
  A complete list showing the ages of Class 1 Referees shall be
forwarded to The Football Association annually.
   C o unty Associations m ay compile a special list of Referees
over the age of fifty (50). previously Class 1 or 2; such
Referees to be classified as Ix or 2x. but their names are not
114                         REFEREES


to be included in the annual return to The Football
Association. The grading of a Referee by a County
Association must be accepted by all the other Associations
throughout the country. (See clause 3 ( b).)
   (b)    When a Referee changes his residence from one County or
Service Association to another County Association the latter
must accept in the first instance the classification of the former
County or Service Association. If, after trial or examination, the
Referee is not deemed to be of the standard of their classified
Referees the County Association may reclassify him.
   (c-) County Associations may re-examine Referees registered
with them when deemed desirable and may remove the names of
 Referees from their register. A Referee who has failed to register
with any County Association for more than two (2) seasons
shall not be re-registered until the application has been
considered by the appropriate Com m ittee of the County
Association within whose area the Referee now resides.
  (d) N o person below fourteen (14) years of age shall be
registered as a Referee.
   (e) Referees under 16 years o f age are only eligible to
officiate as referees or linesmen in C om petitions involving
players o f 16 years o f age or less.


4.     Disqualification
     (a) County Associations must, on removing the name of a
Referee from their List of registered Referees, notify The
Football Association who may take such further action as it
deems desirable.
   ( b) Competitions removing the name of a Referee or Linesman
from their register for any reason must notify the County
Association with whom he is registered.
    (c) County Associations and Com petitions must remove
from their registers the nam e of any Official proved to have
been concerned as an agent for a Club in the transfer a nd/or
engagement or attempted transfer a n d /o r engagement of a
Player.
  (d) Complaints by or against Referees and Linesmen shall be
made to the parent County Association with which the Official is
registered or to The Football Association.
                                    REFEREES                                     115


  (e)    The registration of Referees who wilfully mis-state their
age will be cancelled and they will not be allowed to re-register
without the consent of The Football Association.
  if) R eferees’ Societies or groups of Referees wishing to
arrange matches against similar organisations must first obtain
the consent of the County Association concerned and such
matches shall not be played during the close season. Referees
who do not observe this Regulation are guilty of improper
conduct.
   (g) County Associations must notify The Football Association
if they re-instate a Referee who had previously been disqualified
under this Regulation.
     (h) R e fe re e s re g iste re d w ith an y C o u n t y shall n o t offici­
 a te in an y C o m p e ti tio n o r m a tc h in w h ic h u n r e c o g n is e d o r
 u n a ffilia te d C l u b s c o m p ete .
     (/) W here a League or Competition imposes a penalty,
 punishm ent or disciplinary action upon a Referee (including
 removal from their list o f Referees at a time other than in the
 course o f their norm al annual review) he m ay appeal against
 that decision or action.
    T h e A p p e a l , w hich shall b e c o n s id e r e d b y th e B o a r d o f
A p p e a l o f th e L e a g u e o r C o m p e ti tio n c o n c e r n e d , shall b e

w ithin f o u r te e n (14) days o f th e decision a n d shall be

    (/') If a Player who is also a registered Referee violates the
Laws o f the G a m e to such a degree that a Disciplinary
C om m ittee subsequently imposes a suspension penalty from

    {k) A Referee m ay appeal to The Football Association
against a decision or action o f a C o u n ty Association that
imposes upon him penalty, punishm ent, or disciplinary action

 (including removal from the Association's list o f registered
 Referees). Such Appeal must be received by The Football
 Association within fourteen (14) days o f the decision. The
appeal shall be accom panied by a fee o f Twenty-Five Pounds
(£25), which m a y be returned or forfeited at th e discretion of
the B oard o f A ppeal w ho shall decide b y w h o m the costs of
the A ppeal shall be borne. T he F ootball A ssociation shall
a ppoint the B oard o f A ppeal w hose decisions shall be final
and binding o n all concerned.
    Appeals shall not be entertained with regard to matters
arising out o f the C om petitions o f the affiliated Associations
whose Rules provide that their decision shall be final.


Appointments and Promotion
5. (a) C ou nty A ssociations shall                 act    as    or    appoint a
Referees' Com mittee.

  (b) A County Association may, if requested by a Competition
within its area, appoint Referees to such Competitions or
conjointly with other County Associations for Competitions
em bracing clubs within the area of more than one (1) C ounty
Association.

  (c) To assist the promotion of Referees, Leagues nominated
by County Football Associations shall:—
        (i)     send a n n u a lly a list o f th e officials th e y h a d e m p ­
   loyed w ith t h e m a r k s o b t a i n e d in a c c o r d a n c e w ith th e
   system laid d o w n b y t h e F o o tb a ll A s s o c i a ti o n f r o m tim e
   to tim e (see p ag e s 2 8 2 - 2 8 3 f o r th e spe cim en m a r k i n g
   f o rm ) d u r in g t h e s e a so n a n d a n y o t h e r o b s e r v a tio n s . T h e
   list w o u ld also in d ic a te th o s e R eferees th e y i n t e n d e d to
   reta in , p r o m o t e o r o m it;
      (ii)   apply to County Associations not later than the date
  decided by The Football Association irr each year for the
  nomination o f suitable Referees to fill vacancies on their
  lists.

  (d) Referees registered with more than one (1) County
Association shall receive promotion from their parent
Association.

    (e)     Prom otion from Class 3 to Class 2 and from Class 2
 to Class 1 shall be based on a Referee's practical

 from the Leagues in which he officiated as Referee. All
 Affiliated C om petitions shall obtain from their Clubs a

 accordance with the system published by T he Football
 Association. Subject to Regulation 3 (cO, (e), and ( /) , these
 prom otions shall be open to Referees irrespective o f length of
 service or minimum age.



 Disciplinary Procedure
6. Whenever a Referee cautions or dismisses from the field of
play a Player, he shall prepare in duplicate and within two (2)
days o f the m atch (Sunday not included) send by first class
mail addressed to the Secretary o f the appropriate
Association or such person as is nom inated by such
Association, a report o f the incident or incidents in which the
Player was involved. All such reports shall be m a d e on the
sta n d ard M isco n d u ct R e p o rt F o r m as approved by the
Council an d as m ay be am ended from time to time. T he
Football A ssociation an d C oun ty Football A ssociations shall
ensure th a t Referees are issued with the forms. This
procedure shall apply to L inesm en when such reports are
required.
   If more than one (1) player is cautioned or dismissed from
the field o f play following separate incidents during a match,
separate reports concerning each incident must be sent.
   Referees and Linesmen (if qualified Referees) must attend
Personal H earings when required so to do. If a Referee or
Linesman fails to attend he shall be reported to the
appropriate authority.

o u s c o m p e titio n s .

Overlapping of County Associations
7. W here C oun ty Associations overlap they m ay. subject to
these Regulations, mutually agree about such matters as
registration fees and the ex a m in a tio n ,. registration and
prom otion o f Referees.
   The C ou nty Association which examines or first registers
a Referee shall be known as the parent A ssociation and shall
deal with all matters relating to such Referee. (See 1 ( b).)


M iscellaneou s

follow s:—
        (i) T h e F . A . C h a lle n g e C u p C o m p e ti tio n ;
       (ii) F o o tb a l l L e a g u e M a tc h e s ;
      (iii) T h e F . A . C h a lle n g e T r o p h y C o m p e ti tio n ;

      (vi) P a n e l L e a g u e s ;
     (vii) C o n t r i b u to r y L e a g u e .

    W here release from an appointm ent is required to enable a
Referee to take a more senior appointm ent at least four (4)
d a y s ’ notice must be given to the appropriate Association or
Competition.
    O n ce T h e F ootball A ssociation or a C o u n ty F ootball
A ssociation has appointed a n official to on e o f its m atches, if
th a t m a tc h is subsequently postponed, a b a n d o n ed or results
in a d raw an d the rearranged fixture is then scheduled to take
place less th a n four complete d ay s from the date o f the
original m atch, the Football A ssociation o r C ounty Football
A ssociation appointm ent will ta k e priority over any other

         REGULATIONS FOR TH E CONTROL OF
                YOUTH FOOTBALL

(Players under the age o f eighteen (18) years on first (1st)
               A u g u st in the current season)


  1. A County Association may f o r m a C o u n t y Y outhFootball
Association, or carry out the duties by a Committee of its own
Association.

 2. The constitution of the Youth A ssociation,orC om m ittee,
must be submitted to The Football Association.
           YOUTH RULES FOR THE GUIDANCE
               OF COUNTY ASSOCIATIONS

 The following Youth Rules are for the guidance of County
Associations:—

  1. The Association shall be called ‘‘T h e     County Youth
Football Association.”

  2. The Officers of the Youth Association shall consist of a
President, Vice-Presidents, Chairman, Hon. Secretary and
Treasurer, and Hon. R eferees’ Secretary.

   3. The Youth A ssociation for the purposes of general
m anagem ent shall be governed by a Council consisting of
tw o (2) M embers from each Division elected annually in
accordance with these Rules, four (4) M em bers nominated
by the -------- C o u n ty Football Association, the President,
C hairm an, H on. Referees’ Secretary and the Hon. Secretary
and T reasurer o f t h e      C ou nty Football Association.

    4. All Clubs having their headquarters within.the area of
the — C ou nty Association, the whole o f whose players are
males under eighteen (18) years o f age on first (1st) August,
o f the then current season, shall be eligible for M embership,
subject to the approval o f the Council.

  5. All Clubs upon application for affiliation to the Youth
Association, and at any time thereafter when so required,
shall satisfy the Council th a t they are properly constituted
and also play Football according to the Rules and
Regulations of T he Football Association.

  6. Each affiliated League, C om petitioaand Club shall pay an
annual fee.

   7. Each affiliated Club shall forward on or before the
first (1st) day o f September in each year, to the Hon.
Secretary, a return in accordance with F orm “ A ” in the
Schedule which is annexed to and forms p art of these Rules.
            Y O U T H G U I D A N C E F O R A S S O C IA T IO N S   121


  8. For the purposes of management, the Youth Association
shall be divided into Divisions, geographically as defined by the
Council, the Division to which a Club belongs being determined
by the situation of its ground or, in the event of a Club having no
ground, by the situation of its headquarters.

   9. The Annual General Meeting shall be held not later
than t h e       in each year. A printed balance sheet o f the
accounts, certified by the Auditor, shall be sent out with the
notices convening the meeting fourteen (14) days prior to the
date o f same. Each affiliated League, Competition and Club
shall be entitled to send two (2) duly appointed
Representatives. All Representatives appointed under this
Rule must be Members of the Club they represent. An
individual Member shall only represent one (1) affiliated
Club. The County Officers shall be entitled to vote at any
Ordinary and/or Special General Meeting. Councillors may
attend any General Meeting but may not vote in that
capacity.

   10. [Each County Association will frame its own Rule, as
circumstances may require, to provide the method by which the
Council shall be elected.]

   11. The duties of the affiliated Leagues or Competitions may
be generally defined as follows:—
  To investigate and (if so instructed by the Council) to deal with
reports of misconduct, protests, complaints, or other matters
referred to them by the Council, or by the Secretary in cases
when delay would appear detrimental. The League or
Competition shall, with as little delay as possible, report the
results of their investigations and determinations to the
Secretary. The Council shall have power to amend or revoke any
decision of a League or Competition when they deem it
advisable.

   12. Any Appeal against a decision o f a League or
Competition must be sent to the Secretary, accompanied by a
deposit o f Fifty Pence (£0.50) which may be forfeited to the
funds o f the — County Association if the Appeal is
successful. Members of a League or Competition whose
122        Y O U T H G U I D A N C E FOR A S S O C IA T IO N S


decision is appealed against shall not sit on, or be present at,
the Council Meeting during the determination of such
Appeal. All Appeals under this Rule must be lodged with the
Secretary within seven (7) days of the decision being given,
which it is desired to appeal against.

  13. If an insufficient number of candidates is nominated, the
Hon. Secretary shall report the circumstances to the retiring
Council, who shall elect Members to fill the vacancies.

    14. Five (5) Members o f the Council shall form a
quorum for the transaction o f business. The Council shall
have the power to fill any vacancy that may occur among the
elected Members in their body during the year. The Council
shall have power to appoint such Committees as they may
consider necessary and provide such secretarial assistance as
they think fit.
   [The Rules of t h e    County Association shall apply to all
    matters not provided for in these Rules.]
     MEMORANDUM ON AREAS AND OVERLAPPING
                      OF ASSOCIATIONS

            (Rule 4 of the Rules of the Association)
           (25th August, 1950, and 12th January, 1951)

   1. A County Association is not permitted to alter or extend
its area without the consent of The Football Association.
Consent shall be given only after a Commission of Inquiry is held
at which all parties concerned shall have an opportunity of
attending.

  2. District, Junior and Youth Associations must be
Members of a County Association.

   3. Any District, Junior or Youth Association operating
in two (2) or more Counties shall affiliate to the Senior o f the
two (2) County Associations concerned.

  4. The playing ground shall constitute the Headquarters of
Clubs with the following exceptions:—
   (a) Clubs concerned with Public Offices, Banks, Rail­
  ways, Business Houses and similar institutions;
    ( b)   Clubs which have not a recognised playing ground;
    (c) Clubs which cannot obtain a suitable and convenient
  ground within the area of their County Associations.
  The Headquarters of the excepted Clubs shall be within the
area of the County Association to which they claim to belong.

  5. The Membership of Clubs with Associations which
overlap shall be restricted to the areas determined by the
Overlapping Reports of 1908 and 1927 as follows:—
  Amateur Football Alliance.    See Note 1.
  Army F.A.     See Note 1.
   Birmingham County F.A . Area: The County o f
Warwick and thirty (30) miles from Stevenson Place,
Birmingham (except that part o f the County of

   6. Where Clubs have a Membership with more than one

those concerning Cup Competitions.

Competitions from Clubs having Membership with another
County Association provided the assent o f that Association
has been obtained and it shall have control o f all matters in
connection with the Competitions.

          MEMORANDUM OF AGREEMENT
       BETWEEN THE FOOTBALL ASSOCIATION
        AND THE RUGBY FOOTBALL LEAGUE

   1. Suspension o f a Club or Player by one authority shall
be recognised by the other.

  2. A Club or Player expelled from one authority shall not
be allowed to play under the other for a period o f twelve (12)
months.

   3. A professional Player o f one authority shall not be
allowed to play under the other as an amateur or as a
professional during the same season. The definition o f a
professional shall be in accordance with the Rules o f the
authority to which he belongs.

   4. Each authority shall send to the other lists o f
expulsions, and shall supply any information asked for in
respect o f suspensions.

  5. Clubs shall not be allowed by one authority to take a
name identical with a name held under the other; the term
“Association” or “ Rugby” is not a sufficient distinction.
                              128


                       MEMORANDUM
           SCHOOLBOYS AND SCHOOL GAMES

  One of the important aspects of games in school is the
opportunity they afford of developing a boy’s sense of loyalty
and honour. It is therefore of concern when interest in games
outside the school conflict with a boy’s loyalty to his school
and/or school organisations’ activities.

   1. It is usually the boy o f outstanding Football ability
whose services are sought by any Club, and he is most likely
to be a member o f the school or association team. While
schools matches are often arranged on Saturday mornings
and Club matches take place in the afternoon, it is considered
that a boy should not play in two matches on the same day,
for the one match is likely to affect his play in the other.

   2. An outside Club or organisation should consult the
headmaster before selecting any Schoolboy to play for a
team, and should accept the headteacher’s decision on these
matters.

    Headteachers of schools should not restrain boys, who are
not selected for school games of any kind, from playing for an
outside organisation during their free time.
                               129


                A G R E E M E N T BE T W E E N
         TH E F O O T B A L L A S S O C IA T IO N A N D
               THE FOOTBALL LEAG UE


  The control o f football under the jurisdiction o f The
Football Association within the framework o f The Football
League is carried out by The League under the following
conditions:

  1- The Football League shall have its independent
administration and control o f finance in accordance with its
Regulations.

  2. The President and Members of The League Management
Committee not exceeding nine (9) in number shall be Members of
the F .A . Council.

   3. T h e President o f T h e L ea g ue shall b e a Vice-
President o f th e F .A ., a M em ber o f the F .A . Executive
C om m ittee and a M em ber o f the International F .A . Board.

   4. A Joint Liaison Committee o f members o f the F.A.
and The League shall be appointed each season to discuss
matters o f policy and com m on interest and, where appro­
priate, to make recommendations to the respective
Governing Bodies.

   5. The following procedure shall be followed in cases o f
alleged breaches by Clubs in membership o f The Football
League o f the Rules o f The Football Association or o f the
Regulations o f The Football League:—
  Whichever organisation receives information o f alleged
  breach o f such Rules and Regulations by a Club in
  membership o f The Football League shall at once inform
  the other body. Where a preliminary examination reveals a
  breach o f the Rules and Regulations o f The Football
  Association only, an F.A. Comm ission m ay be appointed
  to deal with the matter in accordance with its Rules.
  Where a preliminary examination reveals a breach o f the
130                       AGREEMENT



   Regulations of The Football League only, The Football
   League may deal with the matter under its own Regulations,
   subject always to the right of the Club concerned to appeal
   against the decision of the Management Committee to an
   appeals body appointed by The Football Association. W here a
   preliminary examination reveals that both the Rules of The
   Football Association and the Regulations of The Football
   League have been contravened, each body shall act indepen­
   dently in accordance with its own Rules or Regulations.
   ( Under discussion.)

  6. All players under written contract must be registered
as such with The Football Association and The Football
League.

   7. Players under written contract shall be placed at the
disposal o f The Football Association at all times in
accordance with the programme o f matches laid down in
Section 8.

   8. The Football Association will endeavour to ensure
that International Matches (Full, ‘B’ and Under-21) will only
be played on the international dates agreed under Clause 11
and that the procedure shall only be departed from in
exceptional circumstances and then only in full consultation
with The Football League Management Committee.
   International Matches at other levels shall be played on
dates mutually agreed between the parties from time to time.

  9. The League m ay play Inter-League Matches with
Leagues o f any other National Association. Such matches
must not be in conflict with International Board Agreements.

   10. League Clubs m ay play with Clubs o f other National
Leagues but these matches must not be in competition with
International Inter-League matches or Representative
matches authorised by The Football Association.

   11. A programme of dates for International and Inter-League
Matches shall be agreed between The F.A. and The League at a
meeting to be fixed prior to the ensuing Season. (Under
discussion. )
                           AGREEMENT                               131


  12. All referees officiating in matches played under the
League’s jurisdiction shall be registered with a County
Association.

   13. The Football Association shall pay to Football League
Clubs providing players and/or staff for the England ‘A ’ or ‘B ’
teams an agreed sum per match. If these payments amount to less
than 25% of the International Match Account surplus, the
balance will be distributed pro rata to the clubs involved,
dependent on the number of players provided. The Football
League are entitled to a full disclosure of all figures relating to this
payment. Payment will be made to the Clubs concerned within 28
days following the said Account being certified by The Football
Association Auditors for the period ending 31st D ecember each
year.

   14. Matters of common interest involving commercial activi­
ties, including the broadcast of football matches, by television,
radio, close circuit, cable, satellite or video, in live or recorded
form, must be negotiated jointly and approved by the Joint
Liaison Committee for recommendation to the respective
Governing Bodies.

other cause whilst under the care or custody o f the Club the

insured value or the cost o f thorough repair in addition to any
other penalty which the Football Association m ay impose.
3.   M e d a ls
   In addition to the Cup, the Association shall present
medals to the players and substitutes in the Final Tie. When a
player taking part is ordered to leave the field o f play for
misconduct, the medal to which he may be entitled m ay be
withheld at the discretion o f the Council.
4.   Control o f Competition

shall be vested in the Council. The Council shall have power
to formulate the Rules o f the Competition and to alter or add
to the Rules as they, from time to time, deem expedient. The
Council shall appoint a Challenge Cup Committee to control
and p a n a g e the Competition on their behalf and to give
decisions on matters arising out o f the Competition which,
within the Rules laid down by the Council, shall be deemed
decisions o f the Council. Clubs shall be bound by any
Contract entered into by the Council in relation to the
Competition. In any matter not specifically mentioned in
these Rules, the Challenge Cup Committee shall have the

12. Provision for Matches Preceding Semi-Final Ties
    For all m atches preceding the Semi-Final Ties, the
following provisions shall apply:—
    (i) Clubs shall not mutually arrange to play a match in lieu
o f a Vase Tie.
    (ii) A ny late kick-off must be reported by the Referee to the
Football A ssociation and the Council shall have power to
impose a fine.
   (iii) In the event o f any match prior to the Sem i-Final
resulting in a draw, extra tim e o f 15 m inutes each w a y shall
b e played, or if, in the op in io n o f the Referee, prevailing
 164     R U L E S O F T H E C H A L L E N G E V A SE C O M P E T IT IO N


       decide at the end o f full tim e and prior to th e com -



     (iv) W hen a first match has been postponed or abandoned
 before the completion o f 90 minutes and neither Glub being at
 fault, it must be played on the same ground on or before the
 following Saturday. If extra time has not been com m enced or
 a match has been abandoned during extra time and neither
 Club being at fault, it must be played on the ground o f the
 Club second drawn on or before the following Saturday
 Matches abandoned through the fault o f the Clubs shall be
dealt with by the Council.
  _ (v) If the match be drawn or again postponed or
 abandoned it shall be played on the following Thursday
unless the Clubs mutually agree to an earlier day and at once
jointly intimate their decision to the Secretary o f the

   (vi)   If a subsequent match is necessary, it must be played
on or before the following Monday.

matches in
the Council
   (viii) When a first match has resulted in a draw, it must be
replayed on the following Saturday unless the Clubs mutually
agree to an earlier day.                          ,
   (ix) If the second match should also result in a draw or
extra time not being completed and neither Club being at
fault, ^ must be replayed not later than the following
Thursday. Unless mutually agreed otherwise, this will be
played on the ground o f the Club winning the toss o f a coin,

In this case, a further replay would be played on the ground :
o f the Club losing the toss. This procedure will be repeated
until a winner has been determined.
    (x)   If a subsequent match is necessary, it must be played
on or before the following Monday.

    (x ii) In a third o r subsequent m atch, C lubs are not
 required to play for m ore than tw o hours.

   Police is assured.

   replacement is available for use if required.

 26. Distribution o f Tickets
 (a) A ll R o u n d s Preceding Sem i-Finals

 (b) Sem i-F inal Ties                                          *
    Where a neutral ground is used for a third or subsequent
 match in a Semi-Final tie, the two competing Clubs and the
 Club staging the match shall be entitled to one-third o f the
 tickets for sale. In the event o f either o f the two competing
 Clubs not claiming or disposing o f its full share o f tickets, the
 residue shall be divided equally between the remaining Club
 and the Club on whose ground the match is to be played.

 2 7. All notices required to be given to the Association by
 any o f these Rules shall be addressed to the Secretary, at the
 offices o f The Football Association, 16 Lancaster Gate,
 London, W 2 3LW.
             RULES OF THE COUNTY YOUTH
             CHALLENGE CUP COM PETITION


 The Competition shall be called “ The Football Association
County Youth Challenge Cup Competition.”

2.   Cup Ownership
    The Cup is the property o f The Football Association Ltd.
    When the winning County Association shall have been
ascertained, T he Football Association shall deliver the Cup
to such County Association, which shall be responsible for its
return to The Football Association on or before the 1st day
o f March in the ensuing year in good order and condition.
    Should the Cup be lost, destroyed or damaged by fire or any
other cause whilst under the care or custody of the County the
latter shall refund to the Association the amount of its current
insured value or the cost of thorough repair in addition to any
other penalty, which The Football Association may impose.

3.  Souvenirs
  In addition to the Cup, The Football Association shall present
souvenirs tQ the players and substitutes in the Final Tie. When a
player taking part is ordered to leave the field of play for
misconduct, the souvenir to which he may be entitled shall be
withheld at the discretion of the Council.

4.  Control
   The entire control and management of the Competition
shall be vested in the Council. The Council shall have power
to formulate the Rules o f the Competition and to alter or add
to the Rules as they, from time to time, deem expedient. The
Council shall appoint a Youth Committee which shall be
empowered to control and manage the Competition on their
behalf and to give decisions on matters arising out o f the
Competition which, within the rules laid down by the
Council,;shall be deemed to be decisions o f the Council. In
any matter not specifically mentioned in these Rules, the
Youth Committee shall have the power to take such action
and impose such penalties as it deems necessary.
                       COUNTY YOUTH C H A L LE N G E CU P RULES



         5   Competition—Eligible Teams
           The Competition shall be on a knock-out basis and shall be
         confined to matches between teams representative of Countv
         Football Associations, each County Association being eligible to
         submit one entry only.                                  5
           All County Associations in England affiliated to The Football
         Association shall be eligible to compete.

        6.   Entry Application—Date and Fee

  (vi) Birth Certificates or other satisfactory proof of date of
birth must be produced for scrutiny by a representative of the
opposing Association if requested providing that such request be
made at least five days prior to the match.
  (vii) Any County Association proved to have played any
ineligible player or to have knowingly contravened any Rule of
the Competition shall be dealt with at the entire discretion of the
Council.
  (viii) A player shall be eligible to play for the County of his
birth, or he must be a recognised playing member of a club in
membership with the County Association for which he is
selected to, play at least 14 days prior to the date fixed for the
playing of any round. Providing he is qualified as above, a player
shall have the choice of the County Association for which he
wishes to play.
   All clubs in current membership with a County Minor
Association are, ipso facto, considered to be in membership
with their County Association.
  (ix) In the case of postponed, drawn or replayed matches only
those players shall be allowed to play who were eligible on the
date fixed for the playing of the round.
  (x) A player who has been suspended may pla^y in postponed,
drawn or replayed ties after the term of his suspension has
expired. *■■■■■ ■


8.   Validity of Qualifications
   If the Council have any doubt as to the qualifications of any
player taking part in this Competition, they shall have power to
call upon such player, or the County Association for which he
played, to prove that he is qualified according to the Rules, and
failing satisfactory proof, the Council may disqualify such
player, and may remove the County Association from the
Competition, or impose such other penalty as they may think fit.

9.   Disqualification
  The Council shall have the power to disqualify any competing
County Association, or player, or players of any competing
County Association, who may be proved to be guilty of any
breach of the Rules of The Football Association.
     174             COUNTY YOUTH CHA LLENGE CUP RULES

  12. Colours
    In all matches prior to the Final Tie, where the colours of two
  competing County Associations are similar, the ‘H om e’ side
  shall change its colours, unless alternative arrangements are
  mutually agreed. In Final Ties both teams shall change their

  13. Laws of the Game
    Except as is provided for in these Rules, the Laws of the Game
  shall apply..

  14. Duration of Matches
    The duration of each match shall be one hour and a half, but if ;
  local circumstances demand it, a minimum of 80 minutes, in
  equal halves, may be played. Any decision hereon must be
  mutually agreed by the competing County Associations, and
  notified to the Referee before the commencement of the match.
  The Referee shall allow for time wasted or lost through accident
  or other cause, and his decision on this matter is not subject to
  appeal.

7.   O rganisation o f the C om petition
   There shall b e a Q ualifying C om p etition and a C om p eti­

Clubs selected by th e C ouncil and exem pted from playing in

w inners o f the Q ualifying C om p etition . T he Q ualifying

     Proper; '■

     R oun d Proper.
   T h e rem aining C lubs shall b e divided into 18 D iv isio n s
geographically convenient, each D iv isio n to co n sist
approxim ately o f four Clubs. T he C lubs in the 18 D iv isio n s
shall com p ete until on ly o n e is left in each d ivision. The
w inners o f t h e 18 D iv isio n s and the 5 0 C lubs exem pt to the

cally con ven ient and then play the First R o u n d Proper. The
w inners and the 3 0 C lubs exem pt to the Second R oun d
Proper shall b e divided into groups, geographically con ve­
nient and shall play the Second R o u n d Proper.

8.'-- T he D raw
    (i) T h e C lubs after having been placed b y the C ouncil in

shall com p ete in the sam e m anner and th is shall be co n ­
tinued until the end o f the C om p etition , w hen the w inning
Club shall hold the Cup.
   (ii) Im m ediately after each draw is m ade, n o tice shall be
given to each Club o f the n a m e o f its o p p o n en ts, and the
date by w h ich the m atch m ust b e p layed. W here alternative

and shall give n ot less than 14 d ays’ n otice o f the date
selected to its o p p o n en ts. Secretaries o f C lubs drawn at

and/or the Final T ies to b e played on a H o m e and H o m e
b asis or it m ay fix th e ground for these T ies.

2 4. Paym ent o f Expenses
(a) Travelling E xpenses
   (i) In all rounds o f the Q u alifyin g C om p etition the
ex p en ses o f the m atch shall include railway fares o f players
and officials o f the visiting Club (n o t exceeding sixteen in
num ber).
   (ii) In the C om p etition Proper the exp en ses o f the m atch
shall include railway fares o f players and o fficials o f the
visiting Club (not exceeding 2 0 in num ber).
   (iii) T h e travelling exp en ses o f the visiting Club to be
allow ed shall be secon d-class railway fares actually paid o f
players and officials from the C lub’s Headquarters.
  (iv) W hen m o to r coach hire is claim ed instead o f railway
fares the charge m u st not exceed the am oun t w hich w ould
have been paid as in (iii) above.

(b) H otel E xpenses
   In the C om p etition Proper, where necessary for the play­
ers and officials o f the v isiting C lub to arrive the night
b efore the m atch o r to com m en ce their outw ard journey
from the C lub’s H eadquarters before 8 am, or they are
unable to arrive h o m e before m idn igh t after com m en cin g
the return journey, hotel exp en ses n ot e x c ee d in g £ 2 0 .0 0 per
p erson per night (n o t exceeding tw enty in num ber) shall be
allow ed if actually incurred.

2 5 . A dm ission to C u p Ties:— Sale o f Tickets
    (i) T h e h o m e Club shall provide for the sale o f tickets

  (ii) A ll m em bers, m u st b e charged for ad m issio n to
ground, en closure and stands in all Cup T ies.
  (iii) T h e price o f a d m issio n for children and senior c iti­

  (iv) T h e prices o f tick ets should be m utually agreed
upon b etw een the tw o C lu bs interested im m ediately after
the draw. A ll q u estio n s in dispute shall im m ediately be
referred to T h e F o o tb a ll A sso c ia tio n for settlem ent.
    (v) T h e m inim u m a d m issio n (except to children and
senior citizens) to m a tch es in the Q u alifyin g C om p etition
shall be £ 0 .3 0 and to all m atches in the C o m p etition Proper
£ 0 .5 0 .
  (vi) A higher a d m issio n charge m ay be m utually agreed
between the C lubs concerned.

2 6 . D istribution o f Tickets
(a) A ll R o u n d s Preceding Sem i-Finals
    A s C hallenge C up R ules.

(b) Sem i-F inal Ties
   W here a neutral ground is used for a third o r subsequent
m atch in a Sem i-Final T ie, the tw o co m p etin g C lubs and the
C lub stagin g the m atch shall be entitled to one-third o f the
tickets for sale. In the event o f either o f the tw o com p eting
C lubs n o t claim ing or d isp o sin g o f its full share o f the
tickets the residue shall be divided equally between the
rem aining Club and the Club o n w h o se ground the m atch is
to be played.

 p r o o f the C ouncil m ay disqualify such player and may

                        LAWS OF THE GAME



        LA W    1.—T H E F IE L D O F PLAY.
        LAW     2.—T H E BALL.
        LAW     3.— N U M B E R O F PLA Y ERS.
        LAW     4.— P L A Y E R S ’ E Q U IP M E N T .
        LA W    5.— R E F E R E E S .
        LAW     6.— L IN E S M E N .
        LAW     7.— D URATION O F T H E GAM E.
        LAW     8.—T H E START O F PLAY.
        LAW     9.— B A L L IN A N D O UT O F PLAY.
        LAW    10.— M E T H O D O F SCORING.
        LA W   11.— O FF-SIDE.
        LA W   12.— F O U L S A ND M ISCON D U CT.
        LAW    13.— F R E E -K IC K (Direct and indirect.)
        LA W   14.— PEN A L T Y -K IC K .
        LAW    15.— TH ROW -IN.
        LAW    16.— G OA L-KICK .
        LAW    17.— CO R N E R -K IC K .

Provided the principles of these Laws be maintained they may be
modified in their application:—

   1.    To players of school age as follows:—
  (a) size of playing pitch;
  (b) size, weight and material of ball;
  (c) width between the goal-posts and height of the cross-bar
from the ground;
  (d) the duration of the periods of play.

  2.     For matches played by women as follows:—
  (a) size, weight and material of ball;
  (b) duration of the periods of play;
  (c) further modifications are only permissible w ith th eco n sen t
of T he International Board.
 208                    LAW S OF TH E GAME



 L aw 1. The Field o f Play
   T he Field of Play and appurtenances shall be as shown in the
 following plan:—

                                     M IN IM U M   SO YARDS




                        PENALTY      AREA

                 GOAL                              L IN E




     1. Dimensions. The field of play shall be rectangular, its
 length being not more than 130 yards nor less than 100 yards’a nd
 its breadth not more than 100 yards nor less than 50 yards. (In
 International matches the length shall be not more than 120 yards
nor less than 110 yards and the breadth not more than 80 yards
nor less than 70 yards.) The length shall in all cases exceed the
breadth.
    2. Marking. The field of play shall be marked with
distinctive lines, not more than 5 inches in width, not by a
V-shaped rut, in accordance with the plan, the longer boundary
lines being called the touch-lines and the shorter the goal-lines.
    A flag on a post not less than 5 feet high and having a
non-pointed top shall be placed at each corner; a similar flag-post
                            L A W S OF TH E GAME                         209

   may be placed opposite the half-way line on each side of the field
  of play, not less than one yard outsidethe touch-line. A half-way
  line shall be marked out across the field of play. The centre of the
  field of play shall be indicated by a suitable mark and a circle with
  a ten yards radius shall be marked round it.
    u3n J hf G o a l ' A r e a - — A t each end of the field of play two lines
  shall be drawn at right angles to the goal-line, 6 yards from each
 goal-post. These shall extend into the field of play for a distance
 of 6 yards and shall be joined by a line drawn parallel with the
 goa - line. Each of the spaces enclosed by these lines and the
 goal-line shall be called a goal-area.
     4. The Penalty-Area.— At each end of the field of play two
  lines shall be drawn at right angles to the goal-line, 18 yards from
 each goal-post. These shall extend into the field of play for a
 distance of 18 yards and shall be joined by a line drawn parallel
 with the goal-line. Each of the spaces enclosed by these lines and
 the goal-line shall be called a penalty-area. A suitable mark shall
 be made within each penalty-area, 12 yards from the mid-point of
 the goal-line, measured along an undrawn line at right angles
 thereto. These shall be the penalty-kick marks. From each
 penalty-kick mark an arc of a circle, having a radius of 10 yards
 shall be drawn outside the penalty-area.
     5. C o rn e r-A re a .— From each corner-flag post a quarter
circle, having a radius of 1 yard shall be drawn inside the field of
play.
    6. The Goals .—The goals shall be placed on the centre of
each goal-line and shall consist of two upright posts, equidistant
from the corner-flags and 8 yards apart (inside measurement),
joined by a horizontal cross-bar, the lower edge of which shall be
8 feet from the ground. The width and depth of thegoal-posts and
the width and depth of the cross-bars shall not exceed 5 inches
(12 cm). T he goal-posts and cross-bars shall have the same
width.
  Nets may be attached to the posts, cross-bars and ground
behind the goals. They should be appropriately supported and be
so placed as to allow the goalkeeper ample room.

International Board Decisions on Law 1
   1.     In International matches the dimensions of the field of
play shall be: maximum 110 metres x 75 metres; minimum 100x
64 metres.
210                 LAW S OF TH E GAME


   2 National Associations must adhere strictly to these
dimensions. Each National Association organising an Interna­
tional Match must advise the Visiting Association, before the
m atch, of the place and the dimensions of the field of play.
  3. The Board has approved this table of measurements for
the Laws of the Game:
                                     Metres
          130 yards                  120
          120 yards                  110
          110 yards                  100
          100 yards                   90
           80 yards                   75
           70 yards                    64
           50 yards                    45
           18 yards                    16.50
           12 yards                    11
           10 yards                     9.15
             8 yards                     7.32
             6 yards                     5.50
             1 yard                      1
             8 feet                      2.44
             5 feet                      1.50
           28 inches                     0.71
            27 inches                    0.68
             9 inches                    0.22 metres
             5 inches                    0.12
              5 inch                    12.7 millimetres
              i inch                    10      millimetres
            14 ozs.                   396 grams
            16 ozs.                   453 grams
              8.5 lb./sq. in         6 0 0 g r/cm 2
            1 5.6 l b ./sq in     1 ,1 0 0 g r/cm 2

   4. The goal-line shall be marked the same width as the depth
 of the goal-posts and cross-bar so that the goal-line and
 goal-posts will conform to the same interior and exterior edges.
   5. The 6 yards (for the outline of the goal-area) and the 18
 yards (for the outline of the penalty-area) which have to be
 measured along the goal-line, must start from the inner sides of
 the goal-posts.
                              LA W S OF TH E GAME                                 211


  6. T he space within the inside areas of the field of play
includes the width of the lines marking these areas.

  7. All Associations shall provide standard equipment,
particularly in International m atches, when the Laws of the
Game must be complied with in every respect and especially with
regard to the size of the ball and other equipment which must
conform to the regulations. All cases of failure to provide
standard equipment must be reported to F .I.F .A .

  8. In a match played under the rules of a competition if the
cross-bar becomes displaced or broken play shall be stopped and
the match abandoned unless the cross-bar has been repaired and
replaced in position or a new one provided without such being a
danger to the players. A rope is not considered to be a
satisfactory substitute for a cross-bar.
  In a friendly match, by mutual consent, play may be resumed
without the cross-bar provided it has been removed and no
longer constitutes a danger to the players.' In these
circum stances, a rope may be used as a substitute for a
cross-bar. If a rope is not used and the ball crosses the goal-line at
a point which in the opinion of the Referee is below where the
cross-bar should have been he shall award a goal.
    T h e g a m e shall be r e s ta r te d by th e R e f e r e e d r o p p in g th e
ball at th e p la ce w h e r e it w as w h e n p la y w as s to p p e d , unless
it w as w ith in th e goal a r e a at th a t tim e , in w h ich case it shall
be d r o p p e d o n t h a t p a r t o f th e goal a r e a line w hich ru n s
p a ra lle l to th e g o a l-lin e , at th e p o in t n e a r e s t to w h e r e th e
ball w as w h e n p lay w as s to p p e d .

a n d m i n im u m d im e n s io n s f o r th e cro ss-b a rs a n d g o al-p o sts,
w ith in th e limits laid d o w n in L a w 1, as th e y c o n s id e r
ap p ro p riate.

     10. G o a l- p o s ts a n d c ro ss-b ars m u st b e m a d e o f w o o d ,
m e ta l, o r o t h e r a p p r o v e d m a te r ia l as d e c id e d fro m tim e to

212                    LA W S OF T H E GAME



   11. “ Curtain-raisers” to International matches should only
be played following agreement on the day of the match, and
taking into account the condition of the field of play, between
representatives of the tw o Associations and the referee (of the
International match).

  12. National Associations, particularly in International
matches, should
  restrict the number of photographers around the field of play,
  have a line ('photographers’ line’) marked behind the
  goal-lines at least two metres from the corner-flag going
  through a point situated at least 3.5 metres behind the
  intersection of the goal-line with the line marking the goal area
  to a point situated at least six metres behind the goal-posts,
  pjohibit photographers from passing over these lines,
  forbid the use of artificial lighting in the form of 'flash-lights’.

Law 2. The Ball
    The ball shall be spherical; the outer casing shall be of leather
or other approved materials. No material shall be used in its
construction which might prove dangerous to the players.
    The circumference of the ball shall not be more than 28 in. and
not less than 27 in. The weight of the ball at the start of the game
shall n ot be m o re th an 16 oz. n o r less th an 14 oz. The
pressure shall be equal to 0.6—1.1 atm osphere, ( = 6 0 0 —1,100
g r /c m 2) at sea level. T h e ball shall n o t be ch anged during the
gam e unless authorised by the referee.


International Board Decisions on Law 2
   1. The ball used in any match shall be considered the
property of the Association or Club on whose ground the match
is played, and at the close of play it must be returned to the
referee.
  2. The International Board, from time to time, shall decide
what constitutes approved materials. Any approved material
shall be certified as such by the International Board.
  3. The Board has approved these equivalents of the weights
specified in the Law:
            14 to 16 ounces = 396 to 453 grammes.
                                 L A W S O F T H E GAME                                 213

to th e r e f e r e e p r io r to th e c o m m e n c e m e n t o f th e m a tc h

  (4) Any of the other players may change places with the
goalkeeper, provided that the referee is informed before the
change is made, and provided also, that the change is made
during a stoppage in the game.
  (5) When a goalkeeper or any other player is to be replaced by a
substitute, the following conditions shall be observed:—
      (a) the referee shall be informed of the proposed
  substitution, before it is m ade;
      (b) the substitute shall not enter the field of play until the
   player he is replacing has left, and then only after having
   received a signal from the Referee;
      (c) he shall enter the field during a stoppage in the game, and
  at the half-way line;
      (d) a player w ho has been replaced shall not take any
   further p a rt in the gam e;
       (<?) a su b s titu te shall be s u b je c t to th e a u th o rity a n d
  ju r is d ic tio n o f th e R e f e r e e w h e th e r c a lle d u p o n to play

L a w 13.       F re e -k ic k

goal).

 C o-operation between Linesm en and R eferee
 W h e n play h a s b ee n s to p p e d th e L in e s m e n s h o u ld as sist the
 R e feree by sig n alling in th e fo llo w in g m a n n e r fo r th e fo llo w ­
 ing incidents:
1 . O ff-side. T h e L in e s m a n s h o u ld lo w e r his flag a t full
a r m ’s length to th e p o s itio n s illu strated , a n d p o in t ac ro ss
th e field o f play to in d ic a te th e sp o t f ro m w h ic h th e k ic k
sh o u ld be ta k en . T h e o n ly ex c ep tio n w o u ld b e w h e re th e
R e feree h a s d ecid ed to p o s itio n h im se lf to ju d g e off-side
w h e n play d ev elo p s f ro m a c o rn e r-k ic k , p e n a lty -k ic k o r
free-kick close to goal.
2. Throw -in. W h e n th e ball goes o u t o f p la y o v e r th e
to u c h -lin e o n his side o f th e field, th e L in e s m a n s h o u ld
in d ic a te the d ire c tio n o f th e th ro w . H e s h o u ld also signal if
th e th r o w e r ’s feet, a t th e m o m e n t o f rele ase o f th e ball, are
in co rrectly placed.
3. C orner and goal-kicks. W h e n th e w h o le o f th e ball goes
o u t o f play o v e r th e g o al-lin e th e L in e s m a n s h o u ld in d ic a te

              KNOCK-OUT COMPETITIONS—
                 OBTAINING A RESULT

    TAKING OF KICKS FROM THE PENALTY MARK

  The International Board at its Meeting on the 27th June, 1970
accepted a proposal by the Federation Internationale de Football
Association that the practice of drawing lots to determine which
of tw o teams in a drawn match should proceed to a later stage of a
knock-out competition or receive the trophy (if any) be
discontinued and replaced by the taking of kicks from the
penalty mark which shall not be considered part of the match,
subject to the following conditions:
  1. The referee shall choose the goal at which all o f the kicks
shall be taken.
  2. H e shall toss a coin, and the team whose captain wins the
toss shall take the first kick.
  3. (a) Subject to the terms of the following paragraphs (c) and
  ( d) both teams shall take five kicks.
      ( b) The kicks shall be taken alternately.
     (c) If, before both teams have taken five kicks, one has
  scored more goals than the other could, even if it were to
  complete its five kicks, the taking of kicks shall cease.
      (d) If, after both teams have taken five kicks, both have
  scored the same number of goals, or have not scored any
  goals, the taking of kicks shall continue, in the same order,
  until such times as both have taken an equal number of kicks
  (not necessarily five more kicks) and one has scored a goal
  more than the other.
   4. The team which scores the greater number of goals,
w hether the number of kicks taken is in accordance with the
terms of the foregoing paragraph (3a), (3c) or (3d) shall qualify
for the next round of the Competition, or shall be declared
winner of the competition, as the case may be.
  5 (a) With the exception referred to in the following paragraph
  (b) only the players who are on the field of play at the end of
  the match, which shall mean at the end of extra time in so far
  as a match in which extra time is authorised, is concerned, and
242     K N O C K -O U T C O M P E T IT IO N S — O B T A IN IN G A R E SU L T


   any who, having left the field temporarily, with or without the
   referee’s permission, are not on the field of play at that time,
   shall take part in the taking of the kicks.
     ( b)   Provided that his team has not already made use of the
   maximum number of substitutes permitted by the rules of the
   competition under which the match was played, a goalkeeper
   who sustains an injury during the taking of the kicks, and who,
   because of the injury, is unable to continue as goal-keeper,
   may be replaced by a substitute.
   6. Each kick shall be taken by a different player, and not until
all eligible players of any team, including the goalkeeper or the
named substitute by whom he was replaced in terms of
paragraph (5) as the case may be, have each taken a kick, may a
player of the same team take a second kick.
   7. Subject to the terms of paragraph (5) any player who is
eligible may change places with his goalkeeper at any time during
the taking of the kicks.
  8. (a) O ther than the player taking the kick from the penalty
  mark, and the two goalkeepers, all players shall remain within
  the centre circle whilst the taking of kicks is in progress.
     (.b) The goalkeeper who is a colleague of the kicker, shall
  take up position within the field of play, outside the penalty
  area at which the kicks are being taken, behind the line which
  runs parallel with the goal line, and at least 10 yards from the
  penalty mark.

   9. Unless stated to the contrary in the foregoing paragraphs 1
 to 8, the Laws of the Game, and the International Board
 Decisions relating thereto, shall, in so far as they can, apply at
the taking of the kicks.
   N.B. In the event of the light failing before the end of the
taking of kicks from the penalty mark, the result shall be decided
by a drawing of lots.

              LAWS FOR SMALL SIDE MATCHES OR
