A PPLICATIONS FOR W ORK PERMITS FOR FO REIG N PLAYERS
          FROM OUTSIDE THE E.E.C. COUNTRIES

This is intended as information as to the procedure to be adopted by Clubs
wishing to register under written contract foreign players Irom countries
outside the E.E.C.                                                     .   ..
   I The transfer agreement negotiated between the two Clubs should
contain a clause that it is subject to an International Clearance Certificate
being issued by the National Association o f the country which the player is
lea\ ing. and subject to the Dep ar tm en t o f Employm ent granting the
application for a work permit.                          . .          .
   ^ Application it) be made to The Football Association requesting the
necessary Clearance Certificate to be obtained from the appropriate
National Association. This should be accom pa nied by a copy ol the
Transfer Agreement and questionnaire completed by the player,
  3,    Applications to he made to the Department of Employment for a work permit
to be granted in respect of the player. Applications should be addressed to the:-
Department of Employment, Caxton House, Tothill Street, London, SW1H 9NF. It
should be noted that work permits are only granted when certain conditions are met.
One of these is that the player concerned must have an established international
reputation.

 T R ANSFER OF PLAYERS BETWEEN THE FOUR HOME ASSOCIATIONS

U nder article 15(4) of the Regulations of F.I.F.A. the Regulations dealing
with International Clearance Certificates do not apply to transactions
between the four British Associations. It is, however, still necessary for a
Clearance to be issued and received when a player moves from the jurisdic­
tion of one British Association to another.
   In this event, the Club which the player is joining must contact The
Football Association with a request for a Clearance to be obtained on
behalf of the player. The player’s registration will not be accepted and he
must not play for his new Club until the Clearance has been received by this
Association.
             REGULATIONS OF PRINCIPLES OF CO-OPERATION
               BETWEEN CLUBS OF DIFFERENT NATIONAL
                ASSOCIATIONS OF THE E.E.C. COUNTRIES

 Article 1
 Contracts concluded between clubs and professional or semi-professional players are
 of a fixed duration and in conformity with the Rules and Regulations of the National
 Associations.
 Article 2
 It must be clearly stipulated in such a contract, that the club is obliged to put the
 player at the disposal of his original National Association for all FIFA and UEFA
 competition matches of his National Representative A Team, without any charges
 whatsoever. The countries qualified “ex officio” for the final phase of a competition
 would be entitled to call their players for six friendly matches spread over two
 seasons. The players must report at the match venue at least 48 hours prior to
                                        APPENDIX                                      301


kick-off. In the event of a breach of this Article, the Association o f origin shall report
the matter to EU F A , and necessary penalties shall be imposed by the Disciplinary
Body appointed by the President of U E F A and consisting of three members o f the
List o f Experts. Its authority shall be limited to the imposition o f fines. Should a
player be unfit, his Club shall be obliged to submit evidence.
Article 3
After his contract has expired, the player shall be free to choose the club with which
he wishes to conclude a new contract.

Article 4
The new club must immediately inform the former club about the conclusion of the
contract. The latter in its turn, in conjunction with its National Association, shall
authorise F IFA , without any delay, to issue the international certificate of transfer.
Article 5
If a player, after having served up to the expiration of his contract, concludes a new
contract with another club, the former club shall have the right to demand an
indemnity o f formation or promotion. In case of disagreement between the parties
the Board o f Experts of U EF A (see Art. 9) decide.

Article 6
The amount of the said indemnity shall be agreed upon by the two clubs concerned
and shall be paid in the currency of the former club, within 30 days from the
authorisation given by the National Association concerned to FIF A for the issuing
of the international certificate o f transfer (see Art. 4).

Article 7
Economic relations between two clubs, as far as the indemnity of formation and
promotion is concerned, shall not be allowed to interfere in any way with the sporting
and/or professional activities of the footballer concerned, who shall be free to play
for the club with which he has concluded the new contract.

Article 8
The agreement concluded by the two clubs must be brought to the attention of their
respective National Associations.

Article 9
If, after the 30 days from the authorisation for the issuing of the international
certificate of transfer, the two clubs concerned have not reached an agreement, either
of them may request that the matter be settled by the Board o f Experts of U EF A
which comprises three persons. The chairman thereof, shall be nominated by the
Executive Committee of U E F A ; while the other two members shall be chosen by the
two clubs concerned, from a list of experts compiled by U EF A . These members,
however, may not originate from the National Associations o f the clubs concerned.

Article 10
In case of conflicts of an economic nature, the clubs concerned may not be brought
Article any aUth0r‘ty 0ther than the Board o f ExPerts mentioned in the preceding
302                                    APPENDIX


Article 11
It is desired that the principles of the national transfer system be adopted, as soon as
possible, to the joint system o f the National Football Associations o f the EEC
countries, defined in this document.


Article 12
A player’s transfer within the period o f validity of a contract will not be subject to
any restrictive regulations provided an agreement is reached between all three parties
concerned: former club, player, new club. However, a club wishing to sign on a
player under contract shall, prior to any other step, inform the club for whom the
player is registered. As long as this imperative condition is not observed, any move,
oral or in writing, direct or indirect, with the player, shall entail sanctions in the form
of a censure or fine up to the exclusion o f the club found guilty from the U EF A Club
Competitions for one or several seasons. The relevant Disciplinary Body shall be
appointed by the President of U EF A and consist of three members of the List of
Experts. The absence of any reply within eight days following the request made by
the club interested in the transfer, shall be regarded as a refusal from the club
concerned to transfer said player under contract.


ENCLOSURE
Operational terms and guiding principles for the activities of the Board o f Experts
with regard to economic conflicts between clubs o f different national Associtions of
the EEC-countries.
Article 1
I. Definition of certain expressions
   a)    List of Experts
         The experts shall be nominated by the Executive Committee of UEFA.

   b)    Player under Contract
         A player who has attained the age of 16 and is registered with a National
         Association which is a member o f U EF A and who has concluded a written
         agreement with a club belonging to one o f the Member Associations of
         U E F A , according to which he is paid for participating in matches and/or
         training sessions in the interest o f the said club.

   c)    Board of Experts
         A Board comprising three Experts (see Art. 1, la), whose function will be
         entirely jurisdictive, and who have been especially chosen, in conformity with
         Article 9 of these Regulations, to settle conflicts or disputes arising in
         connection with the payment of indemnities.
         The decisions of this Board shall be final and not subject to any appeal.

II. a)   A Secretary shall be put at the disposal o f the Board of Experts, Deputy
         Secretaries can also be nominated if need be. The Secretary is appointed by
         the Executive Committee of UEF A.
   b)    The Experts, as well as the Secretary and his deputies, shall treat as strictly
         confidential all matters concerning the settlement of a dispute or conflict,
         with which they have been entrusted during their term o f office.
                                        a ppe n d ix
                                                                                      303

 Article 2
 2 . 1 In case o f a conflict, the Board of Experts shall meet within eight days of receipt
       of the appeal o f the club(s) concerned, in conformity with Article 9 of these
       Regulations.

 2.2 The parties concerned have the right to oppose the presence of a choosen
     Expert, should the said Expert have any personal interest in the dispute or
     conflict.

 2.3 If one of the parties rejects an Expert, in which case the reason for such a refusal
     must be clearly outlined, and if the said Expert does not accept the rejection, the
     Chairman of the Board will judge whether the rejection is justified or not, and his
     decision shall be of a binding nature for the two parties concerned.


 Article 3
 In order to establish the amount of the indemnity of formation or promotion, the
 Board of Experts shall apply as a rule, the following principles:
 - the amount of the indemnity shall correspond to the gross income of the player
   (income earned through his activity as a footballer during the preceding season)
   multiplied by a coefficient factor which varies according to his age.
The gross income shall be composed as follows:
- the player’s fixed wages
- the bonuses paid by the club
- the bonuses paid by the National Association
- the royalties o f the club for publicity made by the player alone, with the outfit or
  the jersey of his club or o f his National Representative Team

                                   Multiplying
Age
18 to   21 years                            12
22 to   24 years                            10
25 to   27 years                            8
28 to   30 years                            6
        31 years                            3
        32 years                            2
        33 years                            1
These multiplying factors represent maximum indemnities such as fixed by the Board
of Experts in the event of disagreement; whereby it is being understood that in said
conditions the indemnity may in no event exceed the amount o f 2 million Swiss
francs.

Article 4
The amount established by the Board of Experts as an indemnity o f promotion or
formation may, m no case, exceed the figure demanded by the former club or the
figure attained by multiplying factors.

Article 5
As soon as the Board o f Experts shall have determined the amount of indemnity, the
debtor club shall immediately effect the payment in the currency o f the creditor club.
304                                                 APPENDIX


Article 6
In case o f a delayed payment, an interest will be charged on the amount due. This
interest will be calculated as of the date F I F A was instructed to issue the
international certificate of transfer. The rate of interest will be decided upon by the
Board o f Experts and will depend upon the interest rate o f the bank in the country of
the creditor club.
Article 7
Fo r amateur players o f more than 16 and o f less than 30 years of age, who become
professionals after having left the country where they were born, in virtue of a
contract concluded with a foreign club an indemnity of formation and preparation
may be claimed from the latter by the club o f their Association o f origin. The club
shall be required to justify its claim by proving its actual involvement in the
formation and preparation of the player.
    If no agreement is reached between the two clubs within the 30 days following the
signature o f the contract, the Board of Experts of U E F A in order to establish the
 amount o f the indemnity shall take as a basis the fixed annual income guaranteed to
the player by his contract as a professional (see multiplying factor for age provided
 in Article 3 o f the Enclosure).
Article 8
The Board of Experts shall further decide upon the distribution of its expenses, by
which it is to be understood that costs incurred by the Experts will be borne by the
respective clubs and that the Chairman o f the Board o f Experts shall carry out his
duties without any charges.

Article 9
If a debtor fails to effect immediately the payment o f an indemnity o f formation
a nd/o r promotion, the Disciplinary Body of U E F A and the National Association
concerned shall impose a penalty on the club. This Disciplinary Body shall be
appointed by the President o f U EF A and consist of three members of the List of
Experts. Its authority shall be limited to the imposition of fines. The National
Association may also take disciplinary measures of a sporting nature.


Berne, June 15th 1981

 334                               APPENDIX



            his last caution. The suspension shall cover all domestic League
           and Cup matches and Friendly matches until such time as his
           Club s recognised senior team has completed the num ber of
           matches appropriate to the punishment in approved Com pe­
           titions during the period covered by its opening match in The
           Isthmian/Northern/Northern Premier/Southern League and
           ending with the final match in which the Club is playing in a
           domestic Competition organised by The Isthmian/Northern/
           Northern Premier/Southern League or the Football Association
           or matches concerning a Club’s County Senior Cup Com pe­
           tition.                                                       '
    (viii) Any period of suspension or part thereof which remains
           outstanding at the end of a Season must be served at the
           commencement of the next following Season.
 (b) Players sent off the Field of Play
       (i) A player who is dism issed from the Field of Play in a recognised
           first team match will be suspended automatically from all
           domestic League and Cup matches and Friendly matches
           commencing on the 14th day following the match in which he was
           sent off and until such time as his Club’s recognised senior team
           has completed three (3) matches in approved Competitions
           during the period covered by its opening match in The Isthmian/
           Northern/Northern Premier/Southern League and ending with
           the final match in which the Club is playing in a domestic
           Competition organised by The Isthmian/Northern/Northern
           Premier/Southern League or the Football Association or
           matches concerning a Club s County Senior Cup Competition
           In addition the player will be fined the sum of £10.00.
      (ii) A player who is dismissed from the Field of Play in a recognised
           first team match for a 2nd, 3rd or 4th time etc: during the same
           Season apart from receiving the automatic suspension and fine
           as in (i) above may be charged under F.A. Rules for "Conti­
           nuing Misconduct” and the Members of the Commission
           appointed to deal with the Case shall have power to deal with the
           player in such manner as they deem fit.
     (iii) Any suspension or part thereof which remains outstanding at the
           end of a Season must be served at the commencement of the next
           following Season.
(c) F.A. Rule 26(a)(x)
   In special cases where the match official’s report indicates a serious
   breach of the Laws of the G am e, The Football Association reserves
   the right to prefer an appropriate charge of misconduct against the
   player. When dealing with such a case the Commission must take into
   account any automatic punishment imposed under the procedures.
(d) Payment to Players under suspension
   Clubs must not pay a Contract player more than his basic wage during
   the period of a suspension.
                                 A PPENDIX
                                                                          335

(e) Re-arranged matches
    A Commission shall have discretionary power to rule that a match shall
    not count towards the completion of a suspension if it is satisfied that
    the game has been arranged by the Club with a view to enabling the
    player to complete his suspension and thus qualify him to play in a
    specific match.

5. DISCIPLINARY ACTION ON CLUBS FOR MISCONDUCT BY
THEIR PLAYERS
(a) Any Club whose players accumulate a total of 200 penalty points or
    more in first team matches during a Season may be required to appear
    before a Commission of the Disciplinary Committee and shall be liable
    to be warned and/or fined for having permitted its players to violate the
    Laws of the G am e in contravention of F.A. Rule 26(n)(i). In addition
    the Commission shall be entitled to order the Club to pav the
    Association the Costs of the Hearing. Any action taken by the Club to
    discipline its players will be taken into consideration by the Commis­
    sion in its findings.
   In so far as the aforementioned Regulation shall apply the following
   points will be recorded against a Club for first team offences:—
     First Team Caution Offences                                   4 Points
     First Team Sendings Off and Players found
     Guilty of Charges under F.A. Rule26(o)(x)                    12 Points
(b) A Club required to appear before a Disciplinary Commission under
    this section shall be represented by at least one of its Directors and the
    Manager.

6. COLLECTION O F ADMINISTRATION FEES AND FINES
(a) It will be the responsibility of the Club Secretary to collect the £5.00
    administration fees from the players concerned and forward them to
    The Football Association when requested so to do.
(b) Fines levied on players must be collected by the Club Secretary from
    the players concerned and forwarded to The Football Association
    when required so to do. Failure to carry out this instruction could lead
    to Disciplinary action against the Club.
336                             APPENDIX


                         SUPPORTERS’ CLUBS

Ref: The National Federation of Football Supporters' C lubs— 744 High
Road, London, N.I7.
   It is ;i long time since groups of ardent followers of football teams
joined forces and formed themselves into the earliest “ Supporters'
C lubs.” Yet those keen pioneers certainly provided the incentive and
encouragement for a mushroom-like growth which plays a major part in
hundreds of clubs today.
    The club must make available to the F.A .. or to the affiliated
Association concerned, a full statement of its accounts, detailing the
amounts and the source of all monies received and the amounts and
estimations of all expenditure.
   The Football Association has no jurisdiction over Supporters' Clubs,
and their relationship with the parent club is entirely a matter for the two
parties to determine.
   Id) The only point which the F.A. makes is that, if the club accepts
donations from its Supporters' Club, then the F.A. has the right to
examine the books of the Supporters' Club.
   (/>) From time to time, the F.A. has made its position clear by
statements such as:—
"T he F.A. has no objection to members of your S upporters’ Club sitting
on the Football Club Committee if they are e le c te d ." and "Footballers
may take part in an organising capacity for a Supporters’ Club Football
Pool."
   If) In granting such independence, the F.A. can fairly claim that its
practice has always been that, if an official of a Football Club becomes an
official of a Supporters’ Club, he does so on the understanding that the
Supporters' Club does not carry out any action contrary to the policies or
decisions of the F.A.
Relationship between a Club and its Supporters’ Club
   («) It must be realised that there is no official link between a.
Supporters’ Club and a Football Club—they are two distinct clubs.
   i h) The Football Club has complete control over the management of its
own affairs, and it is contrary to F.A. Rules for Supporters' Clubs to
interfere in any way with the general running of the Football Club.
  (( ) A Supporters' Club is only an adjunct to the Football Club, and its
main functions are social and fund raising. Such funds may be made
available to the Football Club at the discretion of the Football Club—the
Supporters' Club cannot dictate policy.
  u/) It must therefore be remembered that membership of a Supporters'
Club does not entitle that member to participate in anv wav in the affairs
of the Football Club.

Useful Enterprises
  (til In addition to encouragement at the actual matches, the modern
supporter is prepared to assume a variety of jobs which will, directly, or
indirectly, be of benefit to his club. Such behind-the-scenes enterprises
include the following: —
  li) t he hiring-out of cushions for spectators.

    ^ ^                              LOAN SCHEME
    1. General
    The Football Association will consider applications for loans from Clubs in
 membership with The Football Association, or an affiliated Association, to acquire
 the freehold of a ground, or to develop and improve existing facilities. The considera­
 tion of applications will also be extended to County Associations who wish to acquire
 their own freehold offices.
   2. Details
   (a) Maximum Loan
   The Maximum loan granted shall not exceed £10,000, or two/thirds the value of
freehold property.
   (b) Security
  The security required for a loan must be a first mortgage on a freehold ground, or a
written guarantee given by a local authority where a ground is leasehold. No other
security will be acceptable.
  (c) Interest Rates
  The rate of interest shall be at the discretion of the Committee, based upon the bank
base rate prevailing at the time. The interest shall be payable upon the first and
subsequent anniversaries of the loan.
  (d) Repayment
  The period of repayment shall not exceed ten years and shall be repaid in equal
  nual instalments at the same time as the interest becomes due. Clubs may make
     repayments by monthly bank standing order if necessary.

 6. The state of stands and seating accommodation, stairs, lifts, handrails,

 7. The strength and condition of floodlighting installations including

  For Clubs with grounds with a capacity in excess o f 25,000.
   1. They will comply with requirements ui) (i) and ( b ) I to 9 inclusive.
  2. T hey will, wherever possible, implement the desiderata outlined in(»)
  (ii), (iii) and (iv).
      When Clubs were approached on this subject after the 1946 disaster
  the majority of Clubs agreed that some form of inspection was
  necessary. They felt, however, at that time, that it was impossible to
  draft a set of model conditions to meet all circumstances. They pointed
  out that most grounds were examined by a variety of officials including
  the Borough Surveyor, the Club Architect and the Police.
      It is true that most, if not all grounds, specified above, are inspected by
  some authority. Nevertheless, there must be an individual or an
  authority to give an expert opinion on all the requirements laid down in
  paragraph lb) (1-9) listed above.
      Whilst no attempt is made to define "qualified personnel" they would,
  almost without exception, include a Surveyor and a Consulting
  Engineer.
      Irrespective of whom the "qualified p e rsonnel" are it is directed by the
  Council that the person responsible for collating the inspection reports
  shall be an official nominated by the Club.
     To ensure that such inspection has been carried out annually and that
  the inspecting authority is satisfied that all safety requirements have been
  met, all Clubs in Full or Associate Membership of the Association having
  grounds with a capacity in excess of 10,000 will be required to sign a
 certificate incorporated in the annual return to The Football Association
 (Form A) that all facilities have been inspected by qualified personnel
 and that they hold signed certificates that all safety requirements have
 been met.
    Clubs with a ground capacity less than 10,000 may on some occasion
 find that they anticipate a crowd in excess of that figure. On that occasion
 they should consult with the appropriate local authority and ensure that
 they have the necessary assurances that their ground satisfies, as far as is
 possible, the safety requirements listed above.
    A further clause will be inserted in the annual return (Form A) which
will be signed by the Club Secretary certifying that a safety limit has been
agreed for the ground and stating what that limit is.
    Failure to meet these requirements could result in disciplinary action
being taken against the Club.
    The regulations came into force with the return of Form A on 1st
October, 1970.
   The certificate signed by the appropriate Club nominee shall be in the
following form and shall be available in the C lub’s records for inspection
at any time by an officer of, or a member of, the staff of The Football
Association.

                                ASSAULTS ON REFEREES

             Memorandum relative to proceedings in Courts of Law
             following Assaults upon Referees and ancillary matters
                     to be considered by County Associations

   The subject of this M em orandum is of necessity a very wide one and
              only those matters which it is thought to be o f importance
 • . h h f ^jssoc'atlons and t0 Referees are dealt with. In no sense is it
 lo e r r o n t v " . COmP 'etely t0 T o u t th e a p p r o p r i a t e law but is m e a n t
 to ale rt C o u n t y A s so c i a t i o n s a n d R e f e r e e s as to p o ssib le p ro c e e d in g s
 f ollo w in g a s s a u l t s u p o n R e f e r e e s .                              f               p
    A. It might be appropriate first of all to give a picture of the various
 co n cern ed .SSaU       ^      What ‘h ey inV° ' Ve         S0 f ar   as C o u r t s o f L a w are
   They are:—
     (i) C om m on assault
       (ii) Assaults occasioning actual bodily harm
       (m) Assaults involving grievous bodily harm, and
     (iv) Wounding with intent to cause grievous bodily harm
  (a) Dealing with those assaults known as com m on assaults, they being
such as to be of a trivial nature without bruising or disturbing the skin:__
  Court proceedings in these matters can only be instituted at the
instance of the aggrieved person, namely the Referee. The Referee
complainant must satisfy a Bench of lay Magistrates that he has been
unlawfully assaulted. The Magistrates may inflict upon the Defendant
Player a hne of £50 or sentence him to a term of imprisonment for two
months, he Magistrates also have power to order costs to be paid by the
Defendant Player. Often the assailant is bound over in his own
recognisance to keep the peace. Invariably costs are incurred by the
these n     makes the complaint and it is not always possible to recover

  Footban Disciplinary Committes can far better deal with this type of
assault than can the Courts.
  A Disciplinary Committee can award what proves to be a more telling
punishment than can a Court. It is inadvisable that money should be
spent in taking proceedings for comm on assault and the matter should be
reported by the Referee to the County Association and dealt with in the
usual way.

    (b) The next type of assault is that which occasions actual bodily harm,
 f o r this type of offence the Police have power of arrest upon reasonable
suspicion of the offence having been committed and it is a m atter which
should normally be prosecuted by the Police. The offence comes within
tne category ° f what is known as an "indictable offence" which means
  nat it must be tried by a Jury unless the accused player gives his consent
in which case it can be tried summarily before Magistrates.
344                                A PPENDIX



   The term "actual bodily h arm ” includes any hurt, or injury calculated
to interfere with the health or comfort of the aggrieved person. It need
not be of a permanent nature nor amount to grievous bodily harm. It may
be thought that a broken tooth or a bad bruise might amount to actual
bodily harm. In the case of an allegation of actual bodily harm the facts
should be reported by the Referee to the Police without delay and the
complaint should be accompanied by the name of the guilty player and
the names of such witnesses as can be obtained. T he Referee must also
report the matter to the County Association in the usual way again giving
the names of the Player and of the witnesses, if any, and the County
Association should contact the Police without delay in order to assist the
Referee. If the County Association has taken the wise step of appointing
an Honorary Solicitor it might be wise to request him to contact the
Police to see that action is taken. In the case of this type of assault the
maximum penalty which can be awarded in a M agistrates’ Court is a fine
of £400 or six months imprisonment or both. If the case is heard before a
Jury the maximum term of imprisonment is a term of five years. A referee
would be unwise personally to start proceedings alleging actual bodily
harm unless the Police refuse to undertake the prosecution and even then
he should consult with the County Association. The reason for this is that
if such a case is dealt with before a Jury it would be almost essential for
Solicitors and Counsel to be engaged and this might involve the Referee
in a lot of expense which might not be recovered. County Associations
should not support such a personal charge without seeking the advice of
their Honorary Solicitor to learn what might be involved.
   (c) The third type of case is that which is known as an assault causing
grievous bodily harm and is one where a person unlawfully and maliciously
wounds or inflicts any grievous bodily harm upon any person either with or
without any weapon or instrument. Grievous bodily harm means any real
serious bodily injury but it need not be either permanent or dangerous. To
constitute a “ wound” the whole depth of skin must be broken, a mere
abrasion or separation of the cuticle is not sufficient. It is easier to prove an
actual bodily harm charge as described in (ii) above and the penalties are
the same. Much of what has been said so far as relates to a charge of
causing actual bodily harm applies to this type of case.
  (d) The fourth type of assault is wounding with intent to cause grievous
bodily harm. It is unlikely that this is a type of case which football might
encounter and for that reason it is not intended to say more than it is a
more serious offence than that of grievous bodily harm and the maximum
sentence is life imprisonment.

   B.     Next comes the question of compensation which a Referee might be
able to obtain following his being assaulted by a Player. Criminal Courts
themselves have powers to make certain orders.
  (a)      In a Magistrates’ Court their powers are limited to an award of £400
but it is very rare indeed that anything like that sum is awarded. Indeed
the Referee would be well-advised to think twice before asking a
Magistrates Court to assess an award for damages. Even if an award for
damages is made against the Player it does not always mean that the
amount of the award can be collected from the player.
                                APPENDIX                                345


    (/» If a case goes for trial before a Jury a Crown Court has wider
  powers to make an award of compensation but here again it is one thing to
  obtain an order from the Court and another thing to collect the money.

    (c)   It is always open to a Referee who has been the subject of an assault
 and has suffered damage to make a claim for damages in a County Court
 or High Court but here again having obtained an order for damages it may
 be that the player is unable to meet the amount and as a result of the
 proceedings the Referee is involved in a lot of expense without
 recovering anything, not even his own costs unless he applies for and
 obtains an order for legal aid. To obtain legal aid the Honorary Solicitor
 of the County Association should be consulted. Neither The Football
 Association nor a County Association should be called upon to pay the
 costs incurred in proceedings which have been taken without their
 knowledge and any application for financial assistance must be
 supported by the written advice of the Solicitor to the Countv
 Association whose advice should take into account the chances of
 recovering the money.

   (d)     There is, however, yet one other source from which compensation
can be obtained and this is by making a claim to the Criminal Injuries
Compensation Board. One County has been successful in obtaining
compensation for a Referee from this Board. The Board was set up in
 1964 to compensate victims of crime and violence. Before one can make
a claim under this scheme one has to comply with three main conditions
namely (a) the injury must be one for which compensation of not less
than £50 would be awarded, (b) the circumstances of the injury and
damage must have been the subject of criminal proceedings or to have
been reported to the Police without delay, and (c) the applicant must have
given to the Board all possible assistance, particularly in relation to
medical reports which are required.
  An application is made to this Board by writing to the Board for a form
of application and having completed and signed it by sending it to the
Board whose address is Russell Square House, Russell Square, London
W.C. I. The Board will assess what amount should be paid on the basis of
Common Law damages.
   The advantage of making a claim to the Board is that the applicant does
get the money for the compensation which amounts to about the
equivalent of Common Law damages and the applicant is put to very
little expense. If the applicant is judged to be entitled to a payment, he
receives an immediate cash lump sum payment, whereas other sources
ot compensation often involve a collection by instalments even if the
amount is paid.
   It must be repeated that if it is the intention of a Referee to make a
claim to the Criminal Injuries Compensation Board fo r compensation
the tacts and circumstances must have been reported to the Police
without delay and in this connection the County Association should
assist. County Associations should be advised to seek the advice of their
Honorary Solicitor without delay so that they will be ready if the need for
action arises.
 346                                 APPENDIX


    C. Now comes the very vexed question of whether a football
 Disciplinary Com mittee should suspend a player who is accused of
 assaulting a Referee in a case where Court Proceedings are involved.
       It will be realised that some people who are charged in a Court with
 assault are acquitted. As against this it must be realised that a player who
 has assaulted a Referee might be guilty of further violence in subsequent
 matches if the misconduct allegation is not dealt with. Much thought has
 been given to this matter and the conclusion reached is that there is no
 reason at all why a County Disciplinary Committee should not take the
 necessary steps to deal with a player who is accused of assaulting a
 Referee, in the case of a matter which is being considered by a Court of
 Law in criminal proceedings but the disciplinary hearing must be dealt
 with strictly in accordance with the Rules and great care must be taken in
 listening to and considering the evidence. Any person who is not capable
 ot approaching the matter without bias should not sit to hear the case.
   D. Counties may be concerned as to whether they may be held liable
tor damages for libel or slander. There does not appear to be risk of
substantial damages being awarded if the m atter is dealt with honestly
fairly and without malice. Slander is the spoken word and with certain
exceptions, such as those which might affect a person’s professional
reputation, an award of damages cannot be obtained for slander unless
the person defam ed has suffered some financial loss as a result of the
slander. The position, however, is different in the case of a libel which for
our purposes, broadly, might be very loosely defined as a defamatorv
statement reduced to writing. A film could libel a person.
   The Defamation Act 1952 provides that a fair and accurate report of a
finding or decision of an Association or Com mittee thereof relating to a
member t h e re o f................ ....... such Association having been formed to
promote or safeguard the interests of any game of which members of the
public are admitted etc., etc. is entitled to the protection of qualified
privilege subject to explanation or contradiction. This would apply to a
County Association Disciplinary Committee acting without malice and in
accordance with its Rules.
   Another point worthy of comment is that legal aid is not made available
in cases of libel,or slander. Consequently a person who contemplates
taking legal proceedings to recover damages for defamation must be
prepared to meet the legal costs without the assistance of legal aid

                               ADVERTISING
  Advertising on players’ clothing is permitted by the Football
Association, in accordance with the following Decision of Council:—

                         D E C ISIO N O F C O U N C IL

             relating to clothing of players and match officials

                      July 1988 and until further notice


A)     Introduction

       1) This Decision of Council deals with items that may be carried on
          the clothing of players and match officials. The Rules of Associa­
          tions, Leagues and Competitions may provide that Clubs obtain
          permission from such Association, League or Competition
          before carrying any of the items listed in Section C below in
          matches under their jurisdiction.
      2) This Decision shall remain in force until such time as the Council
         shall vary it. Disciplinary action may be taken against Clubs or
         match officials carrying items on clothing in breach of this Deci­
         sion.

      3) Where the Rules of an Association, League or Competition
         require Clubs to obtain permission prior to placing advertising on
         the clothing o f their players, a new application must be made to
         the appropriate authority each time it is proposed to amend or
         change the advertising. There is, subject to the provisions of
         Section (C) 6 below, no restriction on the number of such changes
         that may take place during the course of each season.


B)    The following items are not considered to be advertising:—
      1) A Club emblem, provided it is of an area no greater than 100 sq
         cms (16 sq ins).
      2) The trade mark or name of the clothing manufacturer or a combi­
         nation of both, occupying an area no greater than 16 sq cms (2.5
         sq ins), to be calculated by measuring around the outline of
         emblem and/or name and to include the space between name and
         emblem if both carried.
      3) Players’ numbers.
     4) The name of a Club, to be worn on the B A C K of its shirts o r on its
        tracksuits.

     5) In the case of match officials, the recognized badge of the approp­
        riate Association and/or Competition.
                                    APPENDIX
                                                                              349


 C)     T he following items are considered to be advertising:—

         1} l h! T mef0: recof nised embIem’ or both o f a company or of one
            or more of its products, to be shown on the F R O N T of shirts and
            on no other clothing worn during the course of a match Such
                     h 8 m 1y °,CCUPy a n area no greater than 200 sq cms (32 sq
            ins), to be calculated by measuring around the outline of the
            advertising and to include the space between words if more than
            one is carried or between words and emblem if both are carried.

      4) Youth teams (ie teams consisting solely of players under the age
         of 18 years on 1 st August in the current season) and School teams

         publicising companies whose products, services or activities
         might be considered detrimental to players of this age.

         of match officials.

         Decision of Council. Such changes o f names will only be permit­
         ted when the team is clearly the representative side of the commer­
         cial organisation concerned ie. a works team or one consisting
         principally of employees of the company.

                                JU N IO R CLUB RULES
   A large number of the County Associations have more than a thousand
clubs in their area, and, naturally, a big percentage of these are junior
clubs. Many of them begin in the humblest possible way, but it is essential
for them to realise that it is necessary to conform to certain regulations. In
effect, the club must be properly constituted.


The First Steps
   (i) Granted this natural eagerness to form a club and to play matches,
the next step is to persuade some keen and responsible person— perhaps a
teacher, a scout-master, a parent, or some ex-player— to assist them to
conform to F.A. regulations.
   (ii) Club rules must be drawn up, affiliation to the County Association
must be arranged, and membership must be organised, however nominal a
subscription.
   (iii) No County wants to reject or over-rule initial keeness; in fact,
information to help embryo clubs is sent out regularly.
   Some years ago, The Football Association, in response to many requests
from Junior and Youth Clubs, drew up a list of suggested rules for
newly-formed clubs. As those rules are still sound and applicable today,
they are printed below for the benefit of young secretaries and
organisers:—

Suggestions For Club Rules
    1. NAME The Club shall be called the “ ......................................................
Association Football Club” and shall be affiliated to the ................................
County Football Association.
    2. OBJECTS Its objects shall be to provide association football for its
members and such social and recreative pursuits as may be deemed
desirable by the Committee. (Any other specific objects should be
mentioned here.)
    2. O F F IC E R S The Officers shall consist o f ................................................
all of whom shall be elected at the Annual General Meeting.
   4. COM M ITTEE The Club shall be controlled by a General Committee
consisting of the Officers a n d ......................................................other members
who shall be elected at the Annual General Meeting.
The General Committee shall meet once p e r ................................................and
the proceedings at such meetings shall be duly recorded in a Minute Book.
At meetings of the General C o m m i t t e e .......................................... shall form a
quorum.
   5. POW ERS O F COM MITTEES The property and/or assets of the
Club shall be vested in the General Committee.
The General Committee shall have the power to appoint such Sub­
committees as may from time to time be deemed necessary and shall
receive reports of such Sub-Committees at its meetings.
The General Committee shall have power to suspend or expel any member
deemed guilty of conduct prejudicial to the good name of the Club.
The General Committee shall have power to fill such vacancies as may
arise in its constitution between Annual General Meetings.
 352                                         APPENDIX



 The General Committee shall have power to declare a seat vacant should a
 member absent himself f r o m .............................................................. consecutive
 meetings without an explanation deemed to be satisfactory.
    6. MEMBERSHIP Membership shall consist o f ............................. play­
 ing and ................................non-playing members. (Any special conditions
 relating to membership should be stated here.)
 Candidates for election shall be proposed and seconded by Club members.
 A register of members of the Club shall be kept by the Secretary.
 [n the event of non-payment of subscription b y ....................................
 membership shall be deemed to be terminated.
 A member wishing to resign shall give notice to this effect in writing to the
 Secretary, such notice to be accompanied by payment of all Club dues at
 that date.
    7. SUBSCRIPTION The Annual Subscription to the Club shall be:—
 (a) Non-playing M e m b e r s ........................
 (b) Playing M em bers..................................
 Subscriptions shall be payable not later t h a n ..................................... annually.
    8. AN NUA L M EETING The Annual General Meeting shall be held
 not ater than                            ................................jn each year. The Secretary
 shall give 21 clear day s notice of such Meeting to all members.
 The Financial Statement and Secretary’s report shall be received by the
 Meeting which will also elect the Officers and General Committee by
ballot, appoint auditors and transact any other business.
    9. EXTRAORD INARY G EN ERA L M EETING An Extraordinary
General Meeting may be convened by the General Committee when
deemed desirable and also upon the written request o f .....................................
members.
The Secretary shall give seven clear days’ notice to all members of such
Meeting at w h i c h ............................................Members shall form a quorum.
    10. FIN A N CE The General Committee shall cause to be kept proper
books of account which shall be audited yearly.
Official receipts for all monies received shall be signed by t h e ........................
The General Committee shall authorise cheques to be signed by at least
two of its Members.
    11. AL T ERA TIO N TO T HE RULES No alteration in these Rules
shall be made except at the Annual General Meeting or at an
Extraordinary General Meeting convened for that purpose and only if
supported b y ................... ..       .o f those present and voting at such Meeting.
Notice of proposed alteration to these Rules must be given in writing to the
Secretary by t h e ......................................................jn each year, and notified to
members on notice of Meeting.
   12. OT H E R BUSINESS Any matters not governed by the foregoing
Rules shall be dealt with by the General Committee, the decision of which
body shall be final and binding.
(Note. It may be found necessary to amend or add to these Rules to meet
specific local circumstances.)

Application to Join a League
  (i)     The next step is to apply to join one of the local leagues and to play
competitive football.
                                A PPENDIX
                                                                         353


  (ii) If the newly-formed club is accepted, fixtures will be made for them
members        ^       adhere t0 the rules of that league, they will remain
   (iii) ° nce, thLey have become affiliated, they may have to play “friendly”
games until they are accepted for league and cup matches. Leagues,
however, are not forced to accept clubs into membership, nor are clubs
directed to join any particular league.
